10067{_}944{_}He stopped and swallowed once or twice, as though his throat was dry, and I saw that his fingers were twitching nervously.
10067{_}945{_}"Did you know her?"
10067{_}946{_}questioned Grady.
10067{_}947{_}Rogers loosened his collar with a convulsive movement.
10067{_}948{_}"No, sir, I'd never seen her before," he answered hoarsely.
10067{_}949{_}"Describe her."
10067{_}950{_}Rogers closed his eyes, as though in an effort of recollection.
10067{_}951{_}"She wore a heavy veil, sir, so that I couldn't see her very well; but the first thing I noticed was her eyes--they were so bright, they seemed to burn right through me.
10067{_}952{_}Her face looked white behind her veil, and I could see how red her lips were--I didn't like her looks, sir, from the first."
10067{_}953{_}"How was she dressed?"
10067{_}954{_}"In a dark gown, sir, cut so skimpy that I knowed she was French before she spoke."
10067{_}955{_}"Ah!"
10067{_}956{_}said Grady.
10067{_}957{_}"She was French, was she?"
10067{_}958{_}"Yes, sir; though she could speak some English.
10067{_}959{_}She asked for Mr. Vantine.
10067{_}960{_}I told her Mr. Vantine was busy.
10067{_}961{_}And then she said something very fast about how she must see him, and all the time she kept edging in and in, till the first thing I knowed she was inside the door, and then she just pulled the door out of my hand and shut it.
10067{_}962{_}I ask you, sir, is that the way a lady would behave?"
10067{_}963{_}"No," said Grady, "I dare say not.
10067{_}964{_}But go ahead,--and take your time."
10067{_}965{_}Rogers had regained his self-confidence, and he went ahead almost glibly.
10067{_}966{_}"'See here, madam,' says I, 'we've had enough trouble here to-day with Frenchies, and if you don't get out quietly, why, I'll have to put you out.'
10067{_}967{_}"'I must see Mistaire Vangtine,' she says, very fast.
10067{_}968{_}'I must see Mistaire Vangtine.
10067{_}969{_}It is most necessaire that I see Mistaire Vangtine.'
10067{_}970{_}"'Then I'll have to put you out,' says I, and took hold of her arm.
10067{_}971{_}And at that she screamed and jerked herself away; and I grabbed her again, and just then Mr. Vantine opened the door there and came out into the hall.
10067{_}972{_}"'What's all this, Rogers?'
10067{_}973{_}he says.
10067{_}974{_}'Who is this party?'
10067{_}975{_}"But before I could answer, that wild cat had rushed over to him and begun to reel off a string of French so fast I wondered how she got her breath.
10067{_}976{_}And Mr. Vantine looked at her kind of surprised at first, and then he got more interested, and finally he asked her in here and shut the door, and that was the last I saw of them."
10067{_}977{_}"You mean you didn't let the woman out?"
10067{_}978{_}demanded Grady.
10067{_}979{_}"Yes, sir, that's just what I mean.
10067{_}980{_}I thought if Mr. Vantine wanted to talk with her, well and good; that was his business, not mine; so I went back to the pantry to help the cook with the silver, expecting to hear the bell every minute.
10067{_}981{_}But the bell didn't ring, and after maybe half an hour, I came out into the hall again to see if the woman had gone; and I walked past the door of this room but didn't hear nothing; and then I went on to the front door, and was surprised to find it wasn't latched."
10067{_}982{_}"Maybe you hadn't latched it," suggested Grady.
10067{_}983{_}"It has a snap-lock, sir; when that woman slammed it shut, I heard it catch."
10067{_}984{_}"You're sure of that?"
10067{_}985{_}"Quite sure, sir."
10067{_}986{_}"What did you do then?"
10067{_}987{_}"I closed the door, sir, and then come back along the hall.
10067{_}988{_}I felt uneasy, some way; and I stood outside the door there listening; but I couldn't hear nothing; and then I tapped, but there wasn't no answer; so I tapped louder, with my heart somehow working right up into my mouth.
10067{_}989{_}And still there wasn't no answer, so I just opened the door and looked in--and the first thing I see was him--"  Rogers stopped suddenly, and caught at his throat again.
10067{_}990{_}"I'll be all right in a minute, sir," he gasped.
10067{_}991{_}"It takes me this way sometimes."
10067{_}992{_}"No hurry," Grady assured him, and then, when his breath was coming easier, "What did you do then?"
10067{_}993{_}"I was so scared I couldn't scarcely stand, sir; but I managed to get to the foot of the stairs and yell for Parks, and he come running down--and that's all I remember, sir."
10067{_}994{_}"The woman wasn't here?"
10067{_}995{_}"No, sir."
10067{_}996{_}"Did you look through the rooms?"
10067{_}997{_}"No, sir; when I found the front door open, I knowed she'd gone out.
10067{_}998{_}She hadn't shut the door because she was afraid I'd hear her."
10067{_}999{_}"That sounds probable," agreed Grady.
10067{_}1000{_}"But what makes you think she killed Vantine?"
10067{_}1001{_}"Well, sir," answered Rogers, slowly, "I guess I oughtn't to have said that; but finding the door open that way, and then coming on Mr. Vantine sort of upset me--I didn't know just what I was saying."
10067{_}1002{_}"You don't think so now, then?"
10067{_}1003{_}questioned Grady, sharply.
10067{_}1004{_}"I don't know what to think, sir."
10067{_}1005{_}"You say you never saw the woman before?"
10067{_}1006{_}"Never, sir."
10067{_}1007{_}"Had she ever been here before?"
10067{_}1008{_}"I don't think so, sir.
10067{_}1009{_}The first thing she asked was if this was where Mr. Vantine lived."
10067{_}1010{_}Grady nodded.
10067{_}1011{_}"Very good, Rogers," he said.
10067{_}1012{_}"I'll be offering you a place on the force next.
10067{_}1013{_}Would you know this woman if you saw her again?"
10067{_}1014{_}Rogers hesitated.
10067{_}1015{_}"I wouldn't like to say sure, sir," he answered, at last.
10067{_}1016{_}"I might and I might not."
10067{_}1017{_}"Red lips and a white face and bright eyes aren't much to go on," Grady pointed out.
10067{_}1018{_}"Can't you give us a closer description?"
10067{_}1019{_}"I'm afraid not, sir.
10067{_}1020{_}I just got a general impression, like, of her face through her veil."
10067{_}1021{_}"You say you didn't search these rooms?"
10067{_}1022{_}"No, sir, I didn't come inside the door."
10067{_}1023{_}"Why not?"
10067{_}1024{_}"I was afraid to, sir."
10067{_}1025{_}"Afraid to?"
10067{_}1026{_}"Yes, sir; I'm afraid to be here now."
10067{_}1027{_}"Did Parks come in?"
10067{_}1028{_}"No, sir; I guess he felt the same way I did."
10067{_}1029{_}"Then how did you know Vantine was dead?
10067{_}1030{_}Why didn't you try to help him?"
10067{_}1031{_}"One look was enough to tell me that wasn't no use," said Rogers, and glanced, with visible horror, at the crumpled form on the floor.
10067{_}1032{_}Grady looked at him keenly for a moment; but there seemed to be no reason to doubt his story.
10067{_}1033{_}Then the detective looked about the room.
10067{_}1034{_}"There's one thing I don't understand," he said, "and that is why Vantine should want all these lights.
10067{_}1035{_}What was he doing in here?"
10067{_}1036{_}"I couldn't be sure, sir; but I suppose he was looking at the furniture he brought over from Europe.
10067{_}1037{_}He was a collector, you know, sir.
10067{_}1038{_}There are five or six pieces in the next room."
10067{_}1039{_}Without a word, Grady arose and passed into the room adjoining, we after him; only Rogers remained seated where he was.
10067{_}1040{_}I remember glancing back over my shoulder and noting how he huddled forward in his chair, as though crushed by a great weight, the instant our backs were turned.
10067{_}1041{_}But I forgot Rogers in contemplation of the scene before me.
10067{_}1042{_}The inner room was ablaze with light, and the furniture stood hap-hazard about it, just as I had seen it earlier in the day.
10067{_}1043{_}Only one thing had been moved.
10067{_}1044{_}That was the Boule cabinet.
10067{_}1045{_}It had been carried to the centre of the room, and placed in the full glare of the light from the chandelier.
10067{_}1046{_}It stood there blazing with arrogant beauty, a thing apart.
10067{_}1047{_}Who had helped Vantine place it there, I wondered?
10067{_}1048{_}Neither Rogers nor Parks had mentioned doing so.
10067{_}1049{_}I turned back to the outer room.
10067{_}1050{_}Rogers was sitting crouched forward in his chair, his hands over his eyes, and I could feel him jerk with nervousness as I touched him on the shoulder.
10067{_}1051{_}"Oh, is it you, Mr.
10067{_}1052{_}Lester?"
10067{_}1053{_}he gasped.
10067{_}1054{_}"Pardon me, sir; I'm not at all myself, sir."
10067{_}1055{_}"I can see that," I said, soothingly; "and no wonder.
10067{_}1056{_}I just wanted to ask you--did you help move any of the furniture in the room yonder?"
10067{_}1057{_}"Help move it, sir?"
10067{_}1058{_}"Yes--help change the position of any of it since this afternoon?"
10067{_}1059{_}"No, sir; I haven't touched any of it, sir."
10067{_}1060{_}"That's all right, then," I said, and turned back into the inner room.
10067{_}1061{_}Vantine had said that he intended examining the cabinet in detail at the first opportunity; I remembered how his eyes had gleamed as he looked at it; how his hand had trembled as he caressed the arabesques.
10067{_}1062{_}No doubt he was making that examination when he had heard a woman's cry and had gone out into the hall to see what the matter was.
10067{_}1063{_}Then he and the woman had entered the ante-room together; he had closed the door; and then....  Like a lightning-flash, a thought leaped into my brain--a reason--an explanation--wild, improbable, absurd, but still an explanation!
10067{_}1064{_}I choked back the cry which rose to my lips; I gripped my hands behind me, in a desperate attempt to hold myself in check; and, fascinated as by a deadly serpent, I stood staring at the cabinet.
10067{_}1065{_}For there, I felt certain, lay the clue to the mystery!
10067{_}1066{_}CHAPTER VII  ROGERS GETS A SHOCK   Grady, Simmonds and Goldberger examined the room minutely, for they seemed to feel that the secret of the tragedy lay somewhere within its four walls; but I watched them only absently, for I had lost interest in the procedure.
10067{_}1067{_}I was perfectly sure that they would find nothing in any way bearing upon the mystery.
10067{_}1068{_}I heard Grady comment upon the fact that there was no door except the one opening into the ante-room, and saw them examine the window-catches.
10067{_}1069{_}"Nobody could raise these windows without alarming the house," Grady said, and pointed to a tiny wire running along the woodwork.
10067{_}1070{_}"There's a burglar alarm."
10067{_}1071{_}Simmonds assented, and finally the trio returned to the ante-room.
10067{_}1072{_}"We'd like to look over the rest of the house," Grady said to Rogers, who was sitting erect again, looking more like himself, and the four men went out into the hall together.
10067{_}1073{_}I remained behind with Hughes and Freylinghuisen.
10067{_}1074{_}They had lifted the body to the couch and were making a careful examination of it.
10067{_}1075{_}Heavy at heart, I sat down near by and watched them.
10067{_}1076{_}That Philip Vantine should have been killed by enthusiasm for the hobby which had given him so much pleasure seemed the very irony of fate, yet such I believed to be the case.
10067{_}1077{_}To be sure, there were various incidents which seemed to conflict with such a theory, and the theory itself seemed wild to the point of absurdity; but at least it was a ray of light in what had been utter darkness.
10067{_}1078{_}I turned it over and over in my mind, trying to fit into it the happenings of the day--I must confess with very poor success.
10067{_}1079{_}Freylinghuisen's voice brought me out of my reverie.
10067{_}1080{_}"The two cases are precisely alike," he was saying.
10067{_}1081{_}"The symptoms are identical.
10067{_}1082{_}And I'm certain we shall find paralysis of the heart and spinal cord in this case, just as I did in the other.
10067{_}1083{_}Both men were killed by the same poison."
10067{_}1084{_}"Can you make a guess as to the nature of the poison?"
10067{_}1085{_}Hughes inquired.
10067{_}1086{_}"Some variant of hydrocyanic acid, I fancy--the odour indicates that; but it must be about fifty times as deadly as hydrocyanic acid is."
10067{_}1087{_}They wandered away into a discussion of possible variants, so technical and be-sprinkled with abstruse words and formulae that I could not follow them.
10067{_}1088{_}Freylinghuisen, of course, had all this sort of thing at his fingers' ends--post-mortems were his every-day occupation, and no doubt he had been furbishing himself up, since this last one, in preparation for the inquest, where he would naturally wish to shine.
10067{_}1089{_}I could see that he enjoyed displaying his knowledge before Hughes, who, although a family practitioner of high standing, with an income greater than Freylinghuisen's many times over, had no such expert knowledge of toxicology as a coroner's physician would naturally possess.
10067{_}1090{_}The two detectives and the coroner came back while the discussion was still in progress and listened in silence to Freylinghuisen's statement of the case.
10067{_}1091{_}Grady's mahogany face told absolutely nothing of what was passing in his brain, but Simmonds was plainly bewildered.
10067{_}1092{_}It was evident from his look that nothing had been found to shed any light on the mystery; and now that his suicide theory had fallen to pieces, he was completely at sea.
10067{_}1093{_}So, I suspected, was Grady, but he was too self-composed to betray it.
10067{_}1094{_}The coroner drew the two physicians aside and talked to them for a few moments in a low tone.
10067{_}1095{_}Then he turned to Grady.
10067{_}1096{_}"Freylinghuisen thinks there is no necessity for a post-mortem," he said.
10067{_}1097{_}"The symptoms are in every way identical with those of the other man who was killed here this afternoon.
10067{_}1098{_}There can be no question that both of them died from the same cause.
10067{_}1099{_}He is ready to make his return to that effect."
10067{_}1100{_}"Very well," assented Grady.
10067{_}1101{_}"The body can be turned over to the relatives, then."
10067{_}1102{_}"There aren't any relatives," I said; "at least, no near ones.
10067{_}1103{_}Vantine was the last of this branch of the family.
10067{_}1104{_}I happen to know that our firm has been named as his executors in his will, so, if there is no objection, I'll take charge of things."
10067{_}1105{_}"Very well, Mr. Lester," said Grady again; and then he looked at me.
10067{_}1106{_}"Do you know the provisions of the will?"
10067{_}1107{_}he asked.
10067{_}1108{_}"I do."
10067{_}1109{_}"In the light of those provisions, do you know of any one who would have an interest in Vantine's death?"
10067{_}1110{_}"I think I may tell you the provisions," I said, after a moment.
10067{_}1111{_}"With the exception of a few legacies to his servants, his whole fortune is left to the Metropolitan Museum of Art."
10067{_}1112{_}"You have been his attorney for some time?"
10067{_}1113{_}"We have been his legal advisers for many years."
10067{_}1114{_}"Have you ever learned that he had an enemy?"
10067{_}1115{_}"No," I answered instantly; "so far as I know, he had not an enemy on earth."
10067{_}1116{_}"He was never married, I believe?"
10067{_}1117{_}"No."
10067{_}1118{_}"Was he ever, to your knowledge, involved with a woman?"
10067{_}1119{_}"No," I said again.
10067{_}1120{_}"I was astounded when I heard Rogers's story."
10067{_}1121{_}"So you can give us no hint as to this woman's identity?"
10067{_}1122{_}"I only wish I could!"
10067{_}1123{_}I said, with fervour.
10067{_}1124{_}"Thank you, Mr. Lester," and Grady turned to Simmonds.
10067{_}1125{_}"I don't see that there is anything more we can do here," he added.
10067{_}1126{_}"There's one thing, though, Mr. Lester, I will have to ask you to do.
10067{_}1127{_}That is to keep all the servants here until after the inquest.

10067{_}1129{_}"I will be responsible for their appearance at the inquest."

10067{_}1131{_}"I want Freylinghuisen to make some tests to-morrow.

10067{_}1134{_}Dr. Hughes lingered for a last word.

10067{_}1137{_}I knew what he meant.
10067{_}1138{_}Already the face of the dead man was showing certain ugly discolourations.

10067{_}1146{_}He has cultivated that sibylline look until people think he's a wonder.

10067{_}1168{_}"Did you ring, sir?"
10067{_}1169{_}he asked.
10067{_}1170{_}He was still miserably nervous, but much more self-controlled than he had been earlier in the evening.
10067{_}1171{_}"Yes," I said.
10067{_}1172{_}"Mr. Godfrey wishes to speak to you."
10067{_}1173{_}It seemed to me that Rogers turned visibly paler; there was certainly fear in the glance he turned upon my companion.
10067{_}1174{_}But Godfrey smiled reassuringly.

10067{_}1176{_}he inquired.

10067{_}1179{_}"All the others, of course.
10067{_}1180{_}They will be storming this house, Rogers, before long.
10067{_}1181{_}You will meet them at the door, you will refuse to admit one of them; you will tell them that there is nothing to be learned here, and that they must go to the police.

10067{_}1186{_}Did you ever see that person before?"

10067{_}1188{_}The latter hesitated an instant, and then took the print with a trembling hand.
10067{_}1189{_}Stark fear was in his eyes again; then slowly he raised the print to the light, glanced at it....  "Catch him, Lester!"

10067{_}1191{_}For Rogers, clutching wildly at his collar, spun half around and fell with a crash.
10067{_}1192{_}Godfrey's arm broke the fall somewhat, but as for me, I was too dazed to move.

10067{_}1194{_}Godfrey commanded sharply, as Parks came running up.
10067{_}1195{_}"Rogers has been taken ill."  And then, as Parks sped down the hall again, I saw Godfrey loosen the collar of the unconscious man and begin to chafe his temples fiercely.

10067{_}1198{_}At the words, I remembered; and, stooping, picked up the photograph which had fluttered from Rogers's nerveless fingers.

10067{_}1200{_}CHAPTER VIII  PRECAUTIONS   But it wasn't apoplexy.
10067{_}1201{_}It was Parks who reassured us, when he came hurrying back a minute later with a glass of water in one hand and a small phial in the other.
10067{_}1202{_}"He has these spells," he said.

10067{_}1247{_}"When I first looked at her, I thought I knew her; but it ain't the same woman."

10067{_}1264{_}"Well!"
10067{_}1265{_}said I, looking at Godfrey.
10067{_}1266{_}"What do you think of that?"
10067{_}1267{_}"He's lying, of course.
10067{_}1268{_}We've got to find out why he's lying and bring it home to him.
10067{_}1269{_}But it's getting late--I must get down to the office.

10067{_}1272{_}"But I fancy he'll be afraid to run away.
10067{_}1273{_}Besides, it is possible he's telling the truth.
10067{_}1274{_}I don't believe any woman had anything to do with either death."
10067{_}1275{_}Godfrey turned, as he was starting away, and stopped to look at me.
10067{_}1276{_}"Who did then?"
10067{_}1277{_}he asked.
10067{_}1278{_}"Nobody."
10067{_}1279{_}"You mean they both suicided in that abnormal way?"
10067{_}1280{_}"No, it wasn't suicide--they were killed--but not by a human being --at least, not directly."
10067{_}1281{_}I felt that I was floundering hopelessly, and stopped.
10067{_}1282{_}"I can't tell you now, Godfrey," I pleaded.
10067{_}1283{_}"I haven't had time to think it out.
10067{_}1284{_}You've got enough for one day."
10067{_}1285{_}"Yes," he smiled; "I've got enough for one day.

10067{_}1289{_}Godfrey's energy became a little wearing sometimes.
10067{_}1290{_}I was already longing for bed, and there remained so much to be done.
10067{_}1291{_}But he, after a day which I knew had been a hard one, and with a many-column story still to write, was apparently as fresh and eager as ever.
10067{_}1292{_}"All right," I agreed.
10067{_}1293{_}"If you see a light, come up.
10067{_}1294{_}If there isn't any light, I'll be in bed, and I'll kill you if you wake me."
10067{_}1295{_}"Conditions accepted," he laughed, as I opened the door for him.
10067{_}1296{_}Parks joined me as I turned back into the house.
10067{_}1297{_}"I got Rogers to bed, sir," he said.
10067{_}1298{_}"He'll be all right in the morning.
10067{_}1299{_}But he's a queer duck."
10067{_}1300{_}"How long have you known him, Parks?"
10067{_}1301{_}"He's been with Mr. Vantine about five years.
10067{_}1302{_}I don't know much about him; he's a silent kind of fellow, keeping to hisself a good deal and sort of brooding over things.
10067{_}1303{_}But he did his work all right, except once in a while when he keeled over like he did to-night."

10067{_}1310{_}I always fancied he'd loved a lady who died--I don't know what made me think so; but anyhow, since I've known him, he never looked at a woman--not in that way."

10067{_}1334{_}I liked the man, and I felt he could be trusted.
10067{_}1335{_}At any rate, I had to take the risk.

10067{_}1337{_}"That I am, sir," Parks agreed, warmly.
10067{_}1338{_}"I was very fond of him, sir; nobody will miss him more than I will."

10067{_}1353{_}"Very good, sir," said Parks.

10067{_}1380{_}There was a certain air of arrogance about it, as it stood there in that blaze of light, its inlay aglow with a thousand subtle reflections; a flaunting air, the air of a courtesan conscious of her beauty and pleased to attract attention--just the air with which Madame de Montespan must have sauntered down the mirror gallery at Versailles, ablaze with jewels, her skirts rustling, her figure swaying suggestively.

10067{_}1385{_}With Parks outside the only door, the rooms ought to be safe from invasion.

10067{_}1389{_}Parks met me in the hall, carrying a cot, which he placed close across the doorway.

10067{_}1391{_}"No," I agreed; and then a sudden thought occurred to me.

10067{_}1397{_}"Then why didn't it work when I opened those windows just now?"
10067{_}1398{_}I demanded.

10067{_}1414{_}I'll see you to-morrow."
10067{_}1415{_}Parks helped me into my coat and opened the door for me.
10067{_}1416{_}Glancing back, after a moment, I saw that he was standing on the steps gazing after me.
10067{_}1417{_}I could understand his reluctance to go back into that death-haunted house; and I found myself breathing deeply with the relief of getting out of it.
10067{_}1418{_}CHAPTER IX  GUESSES AT THE RIDDLE   The walk uptown did me good.
10067{_}1419{_}The rain had ceased, and the air felt clean and fresh as though it had been washed.
10067{_}1420{_}I took deep breaths of it, and the feeling of fatigue and depression which had weighed upon me gradually vanished.
10067{_}1421{_}I was in no hurry--went out of my way a little, indeed, to walk out into Madison Square and look back at the towering mass of the Flatiron building, creamy and delicate as carved ivory under the rays of the moon--and it was long past midnight when I finally turned in at the Marathon.
10067{_}1422{_}Higgins, the janitor, was just closing the outer doors, and he joined me in the elevator a moment later.
10067{_}1423{_}"There's a gentleman waiting to see you, sir," he said, as the car started upward.
10067{_}1424{_}"Mr. Godfrey, sir.
10067{_}1425{_}He came in about ten minutes ago.
10067{_}1426{_}He said you were expecting him, so I let him into your rooms."
10067{_}1427{_}"That was right," I said, and reflected again upon Godfrey's exhaustless energy.
10067{_}1428{_}I found him lolling in an easy chair, and he looked up with a smile at my entrance.
10067{_}1429{_}"Higgins said you hadn't come in yet," he explained, "so I thought I'd wait a few minutes on the off chance that you mightn't be too tired to talk.
10067{_}1430{_}If you are, say so, and I'll be moving along."
10067{_}1431{_}"I'm not too tired," I said, hanging up my coat.
10067{_}1432{_}"I feel a good deal better than I did an hour ago."
10067{_}1433{_}"I saw that you were about all in."
10067{_}1434{_}"How do you keep it up, Godfrey?"
10067{_}1435{_}I asked, sitting down opposite him.
10067{_}1436{_}"You don't seem tired at all."
10067{_}1437{_}"I _am_ tired, though," he said, "a little.
10067{_}1438{_}But I've got a fool brain that won't let my body go to sleep so long as there is work to be done.
10067{_}1439{_}Then, as soon as everything is finished, the brain lets go and the body sleeps like a log.
10067{_}1440{_}Now I knew I couldn't go to sleep properly to-night until I had heard the very interesting theory you are going to confide to me.
10067{_}1441{_}Besides, I have a thing or two to tell you."
10067{_}1442{_}"Go ahead," I said.
10067{_}1443{_}"We had a cable from our Paris office just before I left.
10067{_}1444{_}It seems that M. Theophile d'Aurelle plays the fiddle in the orchestra of the Cafe de Paris.
10067{_}1445{_}He played as usual to-night, so that it is manifestly impossible that he should also be lying in the New York morgue.
10067{_}1446{_}Moreover, none of his friends, so far as he knows, is in America.
10067{_}1447{_}No doubt he may be able to identify the photograph of the dead man, and we've already started one on the way, but we can't hear from it for six or eight days.
10067{_}1448{_}But my guess was right--the fellow's name isn't d'Aurelle."
10067{_}1449{_}"You say you have a photograph?"
10067{_}1450{_}"Yes, I had some taken of the body this afternoon.
10067{_}1451{_}Here's one of them.
10067{_}1452{_}Keep it; you may have a use for it."
10067{_}1453{_}I took the card, and, as I gazed at the face depicted upon it, I realised that the distorted countenance I had seen in the afternoon had given me no idea of the man's appearance.
10067{_}1454{_}Now the eyes were closed and the features composed and peaceful, but even death failed to give them any dignity.
10067{_}1455{_}It was a weak and dissipated face, the face of a hanger-on of cafes, as Parks had said--of a loiterer along the boulevards, of a man without ambition, and capable of any depth of meanness and deceit.
10067{_}1456{_}At least, that is how I read it.
10067{_}1457{_}"He's evidently low-class," said Godfrey, watching me.
10067{_}1458{_}"One of those parasites, without work and without income, so common in Paris.
10067{_}1459{_}Shop-girls and ladies' maids have a weakness for them."
10067{_}1460{_}"I think you are right," I agreed; "but, at the same time, if he was of that type, I don't see what business he could have had with Philip Vantine."
10067{_}1461{_}"Neither do I; but there are a lot of other things I don't see, either.
10067{_}1462{_}We're all in the dark, Lester; have you thought of that?
10067{_}1463{_}Absolutely in the dark."
10067{_}1464{_}"Yes, I have thought of it," I said, slowly.
10067{_}1465{_}"No doubt we can establish this fellow's identity in time--sooner than we think, perhaps, for most of the morning papers will run his picture, and if he is known here in New York at all, it will be recognised by some one.
10067{_}1466{_}When we find out who he is, we can probably guess at the nature of his business with Vantine.
10067{_}1467{_}We can find out who the woman was who called to see Vantine to-night--that is just a case of grilling Rogers; then we can run her down and get her secret out of her.
10067{_}1468{_}We can find why Rogers is trying to shield her.
10067{_}1469{_}All that is comparatively simple.
10067{_}1470{_}But when we have done it all, when we have all these facts in hand, I am afraid we shall find that they are utterly unimportant."
10067{_}1471{_}"Unimportant?"
10067{_}1472{_}I echoed.
10067{_}1473{_}"But surely--"  "Unimportant because we don't want to know these things.
10067{_}1474{_}What we want to know is how Philip Vantine and this unknown Frenchman were killed.
10067{_}1475{_}And that is just the one thing which, I am convinced, neither the man nor the woman nor Rogers nor anybody else we have come across in this case can tell us.
10067{_}1476{_}There's a personality behind all this that we haven't even suspected yet, and which, I am free to confess, I don't know how to get at.
10067{_}1477{_}It puzzles me; it rather frightens me; it's like a threatening shadow which one can't get hold of."
10067{_}1478{_}There was a moment's silence; then, I decided, the time had come for me to speak.
10067{_}1479{_}"Godfrey," I said, "what I am about to tell you is told in confidence, and must be held in confidence until I give you permission to use it.
10067{_}1480{_}Do you agree?"
10067{_}1481{_}"Go on," he said, his eyes on my face.
10067{_}1482{_}"Well, I believe I know how these two men were killed.
10067{_}1483{_}Listen."
10067{_}1484{_}And I told him in detail the story of the Boule cabinet; I repeated Vantine's theory of its first ownership; I named the price which he was ready to pay for it; I described the difference between an original and a counterpart, and dwelt upon Vantine's assertion that this was an original of unique and unquestionable artistry.
10067{_}1485{_}Long before I had finished, Godfrey was out of his chair and pacing up and down the room, his face flushed, his eyes glowing.
10067{_}1486{_}"Beautiful!"
10067{_}1487{_}he murmured from time to time.
10067{_}1488{_}"Immense!
10067{_}1489{_}What a case it will make, Lester!"
10067{_}1490{_}he cried, stopping before my chair and beaming down upon me, as I finished the story.
10067{_}1491{_}"Unique, too; that's the beauty of it!
10067{_}1492{_}As unique as this adorable Boule cabinet!"
10067{_}1493{_}"Then you see it, too?"
10067{_}1494{_}I questioned, a little disappointed that my theory should seem so evident.
10067{_}1495{_}"See it?"
10067{_}1496{_}and he dropped into his chair again.
10067{_}1497{_}"A man would be blind not to see it.
10067{_}1498{_}But all the same, Lester, I give you credit for putting the facts together.
10067{_}1499{_}So many of us--Grady, for instance!
10067{_}1500{_}--aren't able to do that, or to see which facts are essential and which are negligible.
10067{_}1501{_}Now the fact that Vantine had accidentally come into possession of a Boule cabinet would probably seem negligible to Grady, whereas it is the one big essential fact in this whole case.
10067{_}1502{_}And it was you who saw it."
10067{_}1503{_}"You saw it, too," I pointed out, "as soon as I mentioned it."
10067{_}1504{_}"Yes; but you mentioned it in a way which made its importance manifest.
10067{_}1505{_}I couldn't help seeing it.
10067{_}1506{_}And I believe that we have both arrived at practically the same conclusions.
10067{_}1507{_}Here they are," and he checked them off on his fingers.
10067{_}1508{_}"The cabinet contains a secret drawer.
10067{_}1509{_}This is inevitable, if it really belonged to Madame de Montespan.
10067{_}1510{_}Any cabinet made for her would be certain to have a secret drawer--she would require it, just as she would require lace on her underwear or jewelled buttons on her gloves.
10067{_}1511{_}That drawer, since it was, perhaps, to contain such priceless documents as the love letters of a king--even more so, if the love letters were from another man!
10067{_}1512{_}--must be adequately guarded, and therefore a mechanism was devised to stab the person attempting to open it and to inject into the wound a poison so powerful as to cause instant death.
10067{_}1513{_}Am I right so far?"
10067{_}1514{_}"Wonderfully right," I nodded.
10067{_}1515{_}"I had not put it so clearly, even to myself.
10067{_}1516{_}Go ahead."
10067{_}1517{_}"We come to the conclusion, then," continued Godfrey, "that the business of this unknown Frenchman with Vantine in some way concerned this cabinet."
10067{_}1518{_}"Vantine himself thought so," I broke in.
10067{_}1519{_}"He told me afterwards that it was because he thought so he consented to see him."
10067{_}1520{_}"Good!
10067{_}1521{_}That would seem to indicate that we are on the right track.
10067{_}1522{_}The Frenchman's business, then, had something to do with this cabinet, and with this secret drawer.
10067{_}1523{_}Left to himself, he discovered the cabinet in the room adjoining the ante-room, attempted to open the drawer, and was killed."
10067{_}1524{_}"Yes," I agreed; "and now how about Vantine?"
10067{_}1525{_}"Vantine's death isn't so simply explained.
10067{_}1526{_}Presumably the unknown woman also called on business relating to the cabinet.
10067{_}1527{_}She, also, wanted to open the secret drawer, in order to secure its contents --that seems fairly certain from her connection with the first caller."
10067{_}1528{_}"You still think it was her photograph he carried in his watch?"
10067{_}1529{_}"I am sure of it.
10067{_}1530{_}But how did it happen that it was Vantine who was killed?
10067{_}1531{_}Did the woman, warned by the fate of the man, deliberately set Vantine to open the drawer in order that she might run no risk?
10067{_}1532{_}Or was she also ignorant of the mechanism?
10067{_}1533{_}Above all, did she succeed in getting away with the contents of the drawer?"
10067{_}1534{_}"What _was_ the contents of the drawer?"
10067{_}1535{_}I demanded.
10067{_}1536{_}"Ah, if we only knew!"
10067{_}1537{_}"Perhaps the woman had nothing to do with it.
10067{_}1538{_}Vantine himself told me that he was going to make a careful examination of the cabinet.
10067{_}1539{_}No doubt that is exactly what he was doing when the woman's arrival interrupted him.
10067{_}1540{_}He might have let her out of the house himself, and then, returning to the cabinet, stumbled upon the secret drawer after she had gone."
10067{_}1541{_}"Yes; that is quite possible, too.
10067{_}1542{_}At any rate, you agree with me that both men were killed in some such way as I have described?"
10067{_}1543{_}"Absolutely.
10067{_}1544{_}I think there can be no doubt of it."
10067{_}1545{_}"There are objections--and rather weighty ones.
10067{_}1546{_}The theory explains the two deaths, it explains the similarity of the wounds, it explains how both should be on the right hand just above the knuckles, it explains why both bodies were found in the same place since both men started to summon help.
10067{_}1547{_}But, in the first place, if the Frenchman got the drawer open, who closed it?"
10067{_}1548{_}"Perhaps it closed itself when he let go of it."
10067{_}1549{_}"And closed again after Vantine opened it?"
10067{_}1550{_}"Yes."
10067{_}1551{_}"It would take a very clever mechanism to do that."
10067{_}1552{_}"But at least it's possible."
10067{_}1553{_}"Oh, yes; it's possible.
10067{_}1554{_}And we must remember that the poisoners of those days were very ingenious.
10067{_}1555{_}That was the heydey of La Voisin and the Marquise de Brinvilliers, of Elixi, and heaven knows how many other experts who had followed Catherine de Medici to France.
10067{_}1556{_}So that's all quite possible.
10067{_}1557{_}But there is one thing that isn't possible, and that is that a poison which, if it is administered as we think it is, must be a liquid, could remain in that cabinet fresh and ready for use for more than three hundred years.
10067{_}1558{_}It would have dried up centuries ago.
10067{_}1559{_}Nor would the mechanism stay in order so long.
10067{_}1560{_}It must be both complicated and delicate.
10067{_}1561{_}Therefore it would have to be oiled and overhauled from time to time.
10067{_}1562{_}If it is worked by a spring--and I don't see how else it can be worked--the spring would have to be renewed and wound up."
10067{_}1563{_}"Well?"
10067{_}1564{_}I asked, as he paused.
10067{_}1565{_}"Well, it is evident that the drawer contains something more recent than the love letters of Louis Fourteenth.
10067{_}1566{_}It must have been put in working order quite recently.
10067{_}1567{_}But by whom and for what purpose?
10067{_}1568{_}That is the mystery we have to solve--and it is a mighty pretty one.
10067{_}1569{_}And here's another objection," he added.
10067{_}1570{_}"That Frenchman knew about the secret drawer, because, according to our theory, he opened it and got killed.
10067{_}1571{_}Why didn't he also know about the poison?"
10067{_}1572{_}That was an objection, truly, and the more I thought of it, the more serious it seemed.
10067{_}1573{_}"It may be," said Godfrey, at last, "that d'Aurelle was going it alone--that he had broken with the gang--"  "The gang?"
10067{_}1574{_}"Of course there is a gang.
10067{_}1575{_}This thing has taken careful planning and concerted effort.
10067{_}1576{_}And the leader of the gang is a genius!
10067{_}1577{_}I wonder if you understand how great a genius?
10067{_}1578{_}Think: he knows the secret of the drawer of Madame de Montespan's cabinet; but above all he knows the secret of the poison--the poison of the Medici!
10067{_}1579{_}Do you know what that means, Lester?"
10067{_}1580{_}"What _does_ it mean?"
10067{_}1581{_}I asked, for Godfrey was getting ahead of me.
10067{_}1582{_}"It means he is a great criminal--a really great criminal--one of the elect from whom crime has no secrets.
10067{_}1583{_}Observe.
10067{_}1584{_}He alone knows the secret of the poison; one of his men breaks away from him, and pays for his mutiny with his life.
10067{_}1585{_}He is the brain; the others are merely the instruments!"
10067{_}1586{_}"Then you don't believe it was by accident that cabinet was sent to Vantine?"
10067{_}1587{_}"By accident?
10067{_}1588{_}Not for an instant!
10067{_}1589{_}It was part of a plot--and a splendid plot!"
10067{_}1590{_}"Can you explain that to me, too?"
10067{_}1591{_}I queried, a little ironically, for I confess it seemed to me that Godfrey was permitting his imagination to run away with him.
10067{_}1592{_}He smiled good-naturedly at my tone.
10067{_}1593{_}"Of course, this is all mere romancing," he admitted.
10067{_}1594{_}"I am the first to acknowledge that.
10067{_}1595{_}I was merely following out our theory to what seemed its logical conclusion.
10067{_}1596{_}But perhaps we are on the wrong track altogether.
10067{_}1597{_}Perhaps d'Aurelle, or whatever his name is, just blundered in, like a moth into a candle-flame.
10067{_}1598{_}As for the plot--well, I can only guess at it.
10067{_}1599{_}But suppose you and I had pulled off some big robbery--"  He stopped suddenly, and his face went white and then red.
10067{_}1600{_}"What is it, Godfrey?"
10067{_}1601{_}I cried, for his look frightened me.
10067{_}1602{_}He lay back in his chair, his hands pressed over his eyes.
10067{_}1603{_}I could see how they were trembling--how his whole body was trembling.
10067{_}1604{_}"Wait!"
10067{_}1605{_}he said, hoarsely.
10067{_}1606{_}"Wait!"
10067{_}1607{_}Then he sat upright, his face tense with anxiety.
10067{_}1608{_}"Lester!"
10067{_}1609{_}he cried, his voice shrill with fear.
10067{_}1610{_}"The cabinet--it isn't guarded!"
10067{_}1611{_}"Yes, it is," I said.
10067{_}1612{_}"At least I thought of that!"
10067{_}1613{_}And I told him of the precautions I had taken to keep it safe.
10067{_}1614{_}He heard me out with a sigh of relief.
10067{_}1615{_}"That's better," he said.
10067{_}1616{_}"Parks wouldn't stand much show, I'm afraid, if worst came to worst; but I think the cabinet is safe--for to-night.
10067{_}1617{_}And before another night, Lester, we will have a look for ourselves."
10067{_}1618{_}"A look?"
10067{_}1619{_}"Yes; for the secret drawer!"
10067{_}1620{_}I stared at him fascinated, shrinking.
10067{_}1621{_}"And we shall find it!"
10067{_}1622{_}he added.
10067{_}1623{_}"D'Aurelle and Vantine found it," I muttered thickly.
10067{_}1624{_}"Well?"
10067{_}1625{_}"And they're both dead!"
10067{_}1626{_}"It won't kill us.
10067{_}1627{_}We will go about it armoured, Lester.
10067{_}1628{_}That poisoned fang may strike--"  "Don't!"
10067{_}1629{_}I cried, and cowered back into my chair.
10067{_}1630{_}"I--I can't do it, Godfrey.
10067{_}1631{_}God knows, I'm no coward--but not that!"
10067{_}1632{_}"You shall watch me do it!"
10067{_}1633{_}he said.
10067{_}1634{_}"That would be even worse!"
10067{_}1635{_}"But I'll be ready, Lester.
10067{_}1636{_}There will be no danger.
10067{_}1637{_}Come, man!
10067{_}1638{_}Why, it's the chance of a lifetime--to rifle the secret drawer of Madame de Montespan!
10067{_}1639{_}Yes!"
10067{_}1640{_}he added, his eyes glowing, "and to match ourselves against the greatest criminal of modern times!"
10067{_}1641{_}His shrill laugh told how excited he was.
10067{_}1642{_}"And do you know what we shall find in that drawer, Lester?
10067{_}1643{_}But no --it is only a guess--the wildest sort of a guess--but if it is right--if it is right!"
10067{_}1644{_}He sprang from his chair, biting his lips, his whole frame quivering.
10067{_}1645{_}But he was calmer in a moment.
10067{_}1646{_}"Anyway, you will help me, Lester?
10067{_}1647{_}You will come?"
10067{_}1648{_}There was a wizardry in his manner not to be resisted.
10067{_}1649{_}Besides--to rifle the secret drawer of Madame de Montespan!
10067{_}1650{_}To match oneself against the greatest criminal of modern times!
10067{_}1651{_}What an adventure!
10067{_}1652{_}"Yes," I answered, with a quick intaking of the breath; "I'll come!"
10067{_}1653{_}He clapped me on the shoulder, his face beaming.
10067{_}1654{_}"I knew you would!
10067{_}1655{_}To-morrow night, then--I'll call for you here at seven o'clock.
10067{_}1656{_}We'll have dinner together--and then, hey for the great secret!
10067{_}1657{_}Agreed?"
10067{_}1658{_}"Agreed!"
10067{_}1659{_}I said.
10067{_}1660{_}He caught up coat and hat and started for the door.
10067{_}1661{_}"There are things to do," he said; "that armour to prepare--the plan of campaign to consider, you know.
10067{_}1662{_}Good-night, then, till--this evening!"
10067{_}1663{_}The door closed behind him, and his footsteps died away down the hall.
10067{_}1664{_}I looked at my watch--it was nearly two o'clock.
10067{_}1665{_}Dizzily I went to bed.
10067{_}1666{_}But my sleep was broken by a fearful dream--a dream of a serpent, with blazing eyes and dripping fangs, poised to strike!
10067{_}1667{_}CHAPTER X  PREPARATIONS   My first thought, when I awoke next morning, was for Parks, for Godfrey's manner had impressed me with the feeling that Parks was in much more serious danger than either he or I suspected.
10067{_}1668{_}It was with a lively sense of relief, therefore, that I heard Parks's voice answer my call on the 'phone.
10067{_}1669{_}"This is Mr. Lester," I said.
10067{_}1670{_}"Is everything all right?"
10067{_}1671{_}"Everything serene, sir," he answered.
10067{_}1672{_}"It would take a mighty smooth burglar to get in here now, sir."
10067{_}1673{_}"How is that?"
10067{_}1674{_}I asked.
10067{_}1675{_}"Reporters are camped all around the house, sir.
10067{_}1676{_}They seem to think somebody else will be killed here to-day."
10067{_}1677{_}He laughed as he spoke the words, but I was far from thinking the idea an amusing one.
10067{_}1678{_}"I hope not," I said, quickly.
10067{_}1679{_}"And don't let any of the reporters in, nor talk to them.
10067{_}1680{_}Tell them they must go to the police for their information.
10067{_}1681{_}If they get too annoying, let me know, and I'll have an officer sent around."
10067{_}1682{_}"Very good, sir."
10067{_}1683{_}"And, Parks."
10067{_}1684{_}"Yes, sir?"
10067{_}1685{_}"Don't let anybody in the house--no matter what he wants--unless Mr. Grady or Mr. Simmonds or Mr. Goldberger accompanies him.
10067{_}1686{_}Don't let anybody in you don't know.
10067{_}1687{_}If there is any trouble, call me up.
10067{_}1688{_}I want you to be careful about this."
10067{_}1689{_}"I understand, sir."
10067{_}1690{_}"How is Rogers?"
10067{_}1691{_}I asked.
10067{_}1692{_}"Much better, sir.
10067{_}1693{_}He wanted to get up, but I told him he might as well stay in bed, and I'd look after things.
10067{_}1694{_}I thought that was the best place for him, sir."
10067{_}1695{_}"It is," I agreed.
10067{_}1696{_}"Keep him there as long as you can.
10067{_}1697{_}I'll come in during the day, if possible; in any event, Mr. Godfrey and I will be there this evening.
10067{_}1698{_}Call me at the office, if you need me for anything."
10067{_}1699{_}"Very good, sir," said Parks again, and I hung up.
10067{_}1700{_}I glanced through Godfrey's account of the affair while I ate my breakfast, and noted with amusement the sly digs taken at Commissioner Grady.
10067{_}1701{_}Under the photograph of the unknown woman was the legend:       MR. VANTINE'S MYSTERIOUS CALLER       (Grady Please Notice)  And it was intimated that when Grady wanted any real information about an especially puzzling case, he had to go to the _Record_ to get it.
10067{_}1702{_}This, however, was merely by the way, for the story of the double tragedy, fully illustrated, was flung across many columns, and was plainly considered the great news feature of the day.
10067{_}1703{_}I glanced at two or three other papers on my way down-town.
10067{_}1704{_}All of them featured the tragedy with a riot of pictures--pictures of d'Aurelle and Vantine, of Grady (very large), of Simmonds, of Goldberger, of Freylinghuisen, of the Vantine house, diagrams of the ante-room showing the position in which the bodies were found, anatomical charts showing the exact nature of the wounds, pictures of the noted poisoners of history with a highly-coloured list of their achievements--but, when it came to the story of the tragedy itself, their accounts were far less detailed and intimate than that in the _Record_.
10067{_}1705{_}They were, indeed, for the most part, mere farragos of theories, guesses, blood-curdling suggestions, and mysterious hints of important information confided to the reporters but withheld from the public until the criminal had been run to earth.
10067{_}1706{_}That this would soon be accomplished not a single paper doubted, for had not Grady, the mighty Grady, taken personal charge of the case?
10067{_}1707{_}(Here followed a glowing history of Grady's career.)
10067{_}1708{_}It was evident enough that all these reporters had been compelled to go to Grady for their information, and I could fancy them damning him between their teeth as they penned these panegyrics.
10067{_}1709{_}I could also fancy their city editors damning as they compared these incoherent imaginings with the admirable and closely-written story in the _Record_, and I suspected that it was the realisation of the _Record's_ triumph which had caused the descent of the phalanx of reporters upon the Vantine place.
10067{_}1710{_}I went over the whole affair with Mr. Royce, as soon as he reached the office, and spent the rest of the day arranging the papers relating to Vantine's affairs and getting them ready to probate.
10067{_}1711{_}Parks called me up once or twice for instructions as to various details, and Vantine's nearest relative, a third or fourth cousin, wired from somewhere in the west that he was starting for New York at once.
10067{_}1712{_}And then, toward the middle of the afternoon, came the cablegram from Paris which I had almost forgotten to expect:       "Royce & Lester, New York.
10067{_}1713{_}"Regret mistake in shipment exceedingly.
10067{_}1714{_}Our representative will       call to explain.
10067{_}1715{_}"Armand et Fils."
10067{_}1716{_}So there was an end of the romance Godfrey had woven, and which I had been almost ready to believe--the romance of design, of a carefully laid plot, and all that.

10067{_}1719{_}No doubt my own romance of a secret drawer and a poisoned mechanism would prove equally fabulous.

10067{_}1721{_}How Grady and Goldberger would have laughed at it!

10067{_}1724{_}"I've engaged a table at a little place around the corner," he said.

10067{_}1737{_}Some of them thought they knew him and went around to the morgue to see his body, but nothing came of it.

10067{_}1744{_}"Perhaps he hadn't rented a room," I suggested.

10067{_}1762{_}Freylinghuisen says that whoever concocted this particular poison has evidently discovered a new way of doing it--or rediscovered an old way--so that it is at least fifty per cent.
10067{_}1763{_}effective.

10067{_}1769{_}Freylinghuisen thinks it is a new discovery.

10067{_}1835{_}I did so, in silence.

10067{_}1852{_}It's usually turned off in the day-time, but I thought I'd better leave it on to-day, and it rang about the middle of the afternoon.

10067{_}1858{_}It made me feel kind of scary for a while."

10067{_}1881{_}Then I understood.

10067{_}1901{_}"How would he know it?"
10067{_}1902{_}I demanded, incredulously.

10067{_}1906{_}This business was getting on my nerves again.

10067{_}1940{_}"It isn't too late to give it up, Godfrey."

10067{_}1947{_}He pulled back his shirt-sleeves, and placed his electric torch on the floor beside the cabinet.
10067{_}1948{_}Then he paused with folded arms to contemplate this masterpiece of M. Boule.
10067{_}1949{_}"It _is_ a beauty," he said, at last, and then drew out the little drawers, one after another, looked them over, and placed them carefully on a chair.
10067{_}1950{_}"Now," he added, "let us see if there is any space that isn't accounted for."
10067{_}1951{_}He took from his pocket a folding rule of ivory, opened it, and began a series of measurements so searching and intricate that half an hour passed without a word being spoken.
10067{_}1952{_}Then he pulled up another chair, and sat down beside me.
10067{_}1953{_}"I seem to be pretty much up against it," he said, "no doubt just as the designer of the cabinet would wish me to be.
10067{_}1954{_}The whole bottom of the desk is inclosed, and those three little drawers take up only a small part of the space.
10067{_}1955{_}Then the back of the cabinet seems to be double--at least, there's a space of three inches I can't account for.
10067{_}1956{_}So there's room for a dozen secret drawers, if the Montespan required so many.

10067{_}1958{_}He adjusted the steel gauntlet carefully to his right hand and sat down on the floor before the cabinet.

10067{_}1960{_}"If there is any spot I miss, tell me of it."
10067{_}1961{_}He ran his fingers up and down the graceful legs, carefully feeling every inequality of the elaborate bronze ornamentation.
10067{_}1962{_}Particularly did his fingers linger on every boss and point, striving to push it in or move it up or down; but they were all immovable.
10067{_}1963{_}Then he examined the bottom of the table minutely, using his torch to illumine every crevice; but again without result.
10067{_}1964{_}Another half hour passed so, and when at last he came out from under the table, his face was dripping with sweat.

10067{_}1970{_}It's the Louis Fourteenth ideal of beauty--splendour carried to the nth degree.

10067{_}1972{_}And the engraving--nothing cut-and-dried about that.
10067{_}1973{_}It was done by a burin in the hands of a master--perhaps by Boule himself.

10067{_}1977{_}"That's true," he agreed.

10067{_}1980{_}He inserted his hand into the space from which he had taken them, and examined it carefully.
10067{_}1981{_}Then, inch by inch, he ran his fingers over the bosses and arabesques with which the sides and top of the table were incrusted.

10067{_}1983{_}Once I thought he had found the drawer, for a piece of inlay at the side of the table seemed to give a little under the pressure of his fingers; but no hidden spring was touched; no drawer sprang open; no poisoned fangs descended.
10067{_}1984{_}"Well," said Godfrey, sitting back in his chair at last, and wiping his face again, "there's so much done.
10067{_}1985{_}If there is any secret drawer in the lower part of the cabinet, it is mighty cleverly concealed.
10067{_}1986{_}Now we'll try the upper part."
10067{_}1987{_}The upper part of the cabinet consisted of a series of drawers, rising one above the other, and terminated by a triangular pediment, its tympanum ornamented with some beautiful little bronzes.
10067{_}1988{_}The drawers themselves were concealed by two doors, opening in the centre, and covered with a most intricate design of arabesqued incrustations.
10067{_}1989{_}"If there is a secret drawer here," said Godfrey, "it is somewhere in the back, where there seems to be a hollow space.
10067{_}1990{_}But to discover the combination...."  He ran his fingers over the inlay, and then, struck by a sudden thought, tested each of the little figures along the tympanum, but they were all set solidly in place.
10067{_}1991{_}"There's one thing sure," he said, "the combination, whatever it is, is of such a nature that it could not be discovered accidentally--by a person leaning on the cabinet, for instance.
10067{_}1992{_}It isn't a question of merely touching a spring; it is probably a question of releasing a series of levers, which must be worked in a certain order, or the drawer won't open.
10067{_}1993{_}I'm afraid we are up against it."
10067{_}1994{_}"I can't pretend I'm sorry," I said, with a sigh of relief.
10067{_}1995{_}"As far as I am concerned, I'm perfectly willing that the drawer should go undiscovered."
10067{_}1996{_}"Well, I am not!"
10067{_}1997{_}retorted Godfrey, curtly, and he sat regarding the cabinet with puckered brows.
10067{_}1998{_}Then he rose and began tapping at the back.
10067{_}1999{_}I don't know what it was--for I was conscious of no noise--but some mysterious attraction drew my eyes to the window at the farther side of the room.
10067{_}2000{_}Near the top of the wooden shutter, which Parks and I had put in place, was a small semi-circular opening, to allow the passage of a little light, perhaps, and peering through this opening were two eyes--two burning eyes....
10067{_}2001{_}They were fixed upon Godfrey with such feverish intentness that they did not see my glance, and I lowered my head instantly.
10067{_}2002{_}"Godfrey," I said, in a shaking voice, "don't look up; don't move your head; but there is some one peering through the hole in the shutter opposite us."
10067{_}2003{_}Godfrey did not answer for quite a minute, but kept calmly on with his examination of the cabinet.
10067{_}2004{_}"Did he see you look at him?"
10067{_}2005{_}he asked, at last.
10067{_}2006{_}"No, he was looking at you, with his eyes almost starting out of his head.
10067{_}2007{_}I never saw such eyes!"
10067{_}2008{_}"Did you see anything of his face?"
10067{_}2009{_}"No, the hole is too small.
10067{_}2010{_}I fancy I saw the fingers of one hand, which he had thrust through to steady himself."
10067{_}2011{_}"How high is the hole?"
10067{_}2012{_}"Near the top of the window."
10067{_}2013{_}Godfrey came back to his chair a moment later, sat down in it, and passed his handkerchief slowly over his face.
10067{_}2014{_}Then he leaned forward, apparently to examine the legs of the cabinet.
10067{_}2015{_}"I saw him," he said.
10067{_}2016{_}"Or, rather, I saw his eyes.
10067{_}2017{_}Rather fierce, aren't they?"
10067{_}2018{_}"They're a tiger's eyes," I said, with conviction.
10067{_}2019{_}"Well, there is no use going ahead with this while he is out there.
10067{_}2020{_}Even if we found the drawer, we'd both be dead an instant later."
10067{_}2021{_}"You mean he'd kill us?"
10067{_}2022{_}"He would shoot us instantly.
10067{_}2023{_}Imagine what a sensation that would make, Lester.
10067{_}2024{_}Parks hears two pistol shots, rushes in and finds us lying here dead.
10067{_}2025{_}Grady would have a convulsion--and we should both be famous for a few days."
10067{_}2026{_}"I'll seek fame in some other way," I said drily.
10067{_}2027{_}"What are you going to do about it?"
10067{_}2028{_}"We've got to try to capture him; and if we do--well, we shall have the fame all right!
10067{_}2029{_}But it's a good deal like trying to pick up a scorpion--we're pretty sure to get hurt.
10067{_}2030{_}If that fellow out there is who I think he is, he's about the most dangerous man on earth."
10067{_}2031{_}He went on tapping the surface of the cabinet.
10067{_}2032{_}As for me, I would have given anything for another look at those gleaming eyes.
10067{_}2033{_}They seemed to be burning into me; hot flashes were shooting up and down my back.
10067{_}2034{_}"Why can't I go out as though I were going after something," I suggested.
10067{_}2035{_}"Then Parks and I could charge around the corner and get him."
10067{_}2036{_}"You wouldn't get him, he'd get you.
10067{_}2037{_}You wouldn't have a chance on earth.
10067{_}2038{_}If there is a window upstairs over that one, you might drop something out on him, or borrow Parks's pistol and shoot him--"  "That would be pretty cowardly, wouldn't it?"
10067{_}2039{_}I suggested, mildly.
10067{_}2040{_}"My dear Lester," Godfrey protested, "when you attack a poisonous snake, you don't do it with bare hands, do you?"
10067{_}2041{_}I couldn't help it--I glanced again at the window....  "He's gone!"
10067{_}2042{_}I cried.
10067{_}2043{_}Godfrey was at the window in two steps.
10067{_}2044{_}"Look at that!"
10067{_}2045{_}he said, "and then tell me he isn't a genius!"
10067{_}2046{_}I followed the direction of his pointing finger and saw that, just opposite the opening in the shutter, a little hole had been cut in the window-pane.
10067{_}2047{_}"That fellow foresees everything," said Godfrey, with enthusiasm.
10067{_}2048{_}"He probably cut that hole as soon as it was dark.
10067{_}2049{_}He must have guessed we were going to examine the cabinet to-night--and he wanted not only to see, but to hear.
10067{_}2050{_}He heard everything we said, Lester!"
10067{_}2051{_}"Let's go after him!"
10067{_}2052{_}I cried, and, without waiting for an answer, I sprang across the ante-room and snatched open the door which led into the hall.
10067{_}2053{_}Parks and Rogers were sitting on the couch just outside and I never saw two men more thoroughly frightened.
10067{_}2054{_}"For God's sake, Mr.
10067{_}2055{_}Lester!"
10067{_}2056{_}gasped Rogers, and stopped, his hand at his throat.
10067{_}2057{_}"Is it Mr.
10067{_}2058{_}Godfrey?"

10067{_}2060{_}"There's a man outside.
10067{_}2061{_}Got your pistol, Parks?"
10067{_}2062{_}"Yes, sir," and he took it from his pocket.
10067{_}2063{_}I snatched it from him, opened the front door, leaped the railing, and stole along the house to the corner.
10067{_}2064{_}Then, taking my courage in both hands, I charged around it.
10067{_}2065{_}There was no one in sight; but from somewhere near at hand came a burst of mocking laughter.
10067{_}2066{_}CHAPTER XII  GODFREY IS FRIGHTENED   I was still staring about me, that mocking laughter in my ears, when Godfrey joined me.
10067{_}2067{_}"He got away, of course," he said coolly.
10067{_}2068{_}"Yes, and I heard him laugh!"
10067{_}2069{_}I cried.
10067{_}2070{_}Godfrey looked at me quickly.
10067{_}2071{_}"Come, Lester," he said, soothingly, "don't let your nerves run away with you."
10067{_}2072{_}"It wasn't my nerves," I protested, a little hotly.
10067{_}2073{_}"I heard it quite plainly.
10067{_}2074{_}He can't be far away."
10067{_}2075{_}"Too far for us to catch him," Godfrey retorted, and, torch in hand, proceeded to examine the window-sill and the ground beneath it.
10067{_}2076{_}"There is where he stood," he added, and the marks on the sill were evident enough.
10067{_}2077{_}"Of course he had his line of retreat blocked out," and he flashed his torch back and forth across the grass, but the turf was so close that no trace of footsteps was visible.
10067{_}2078{_}We went slowly back to the house, and Godfrey sat down again to a contemplation of the cabinet.
10067{_}2079{_}"It's too much for me," he said, at last.
10067{_}2080{_}"The only way I can find that drawer, I'm afraid, is with an axe.
10067{_}2081{_}But I don't want to smash the thing to pieces--"  "I should say not!
10067{_}2082{_}It would be like smashing the Venus de Milo."
10067{_}2083{_}"Hardly so bad as that.
10067{_}2084{_}But we won't smash it yet awhile.
10067{_}2085{_}I'm going to look up the subject of secret drawers--perhaps I'll stumble upon something that will help me."
10067{_}2086{_}"And then, of course," I said, disconsolately, "it is quite possible that there isn't any such drawer at all."
10067{_}2087{_}But Godfrey shook his head decidedly.
10067{_}2088{_}"I don't agree with you there, Lester.
10067{_}2089{_}I'll wager that fellow who was looking in at us could find it in a minute."

10067{_}2091{_}"He had reason to be," Godfrey rejoined grimly.

10067{_}2094{_}"Those shutters are pretty strong," I pointed out.
10067{_}2095{_}"And Parks is no fool."
10067{_}2096{_}"Yes," agreed Godfrey, "the shutters are pretty strong--they might keep him out for ten minutes--scarcely longer than that.
10067{_}2097{_}As for Parks, he wouldn't last ten seconds.
10067{_}2098{_}You don't seem to understand the extraordinary character of this fellow."
10067{_}2099{_}"During your period of exaltation last night," I reminded him, "you referred to him as the greatest criminal of modern times."
10067{_}2100{_}"Well," smiled Godfrey, "perhaps that _was_ a little exaggerated.
10067{_}2101{_}Suppose we say one of the greatest--great enough, surely, to walk all around us, if we aren't on guard.
10067{_}2102{_}I think I would better drop a word to Simmonds and get him to send down a couple of men to watch the house.
10067{_}2103{_}With them outside, and Parks on the inside, it ought to be fairly safe."
10067{_}2104{_}"I should think so!"
10067{_}2105{_}I said.
10067{_}2106{_}"One would imagine you were getting ready to repel an army.

10067{_}2112{_}He went to the 'phone, while I sat down again and looked at the cabinet in a kind of stupefaction.
10067{_}2113{_}What was the intrigue, of which it seemed to be the centre?
10067{_}2114{_}Who was this man, that Godfrey should consider him so formidable?
10067{_}2115{_}Why should he have chosen Philip Vantine for a victim?

10067{_}2118{_}"Simmonds is sending two of his best men to watch the house."
10067{_}2119{_}He stood for a moment gazing down at the cabinet.

10067{_}2121{_}"I have left the gauntlet there on the chair, so if you feel like having a try yourself, Lester...."  "Heaven forbid!"
10067{_}2122{_}I protested.
10067{_}2123{_}"But perhaps I would better tell Parks to let you in.
10067{_}2124{_}I hope I won't find you a corpse here, Godfrey!"
10067{_}2125{_}"So do I!
10067{_}2126{_}But I don't believe you will.
10067{_}2127{_}Yes, tell Parks to let me in whenever I come around.
10067{_}2128{_}And now about Rogers."
10067{_}2129{_}"What about him?"
10067{_}2130{_}"I rather thought I might want to grill him to-night.
10067{_}2131{_}But perhaps I would better wait till I get a little more to go on."
10067{_}2132{_}He paused for a moment's thought.
10067{_}2133{_}"Yes; I'll wait," he said, finally.
10067{_}2134{_}"I don't want to run any risk of failing."
10067{_}2135{_}We went out into the hall together, and I told Parks to admit Godfrey, whenever he wished to enter.
10067{_}2136{_}Rogers was still sitting on the cot, looking so crushed and sorrowful that I could not help pitying him.
10067{_}2137{_}I began to think that, if he were left to himself a day or two longer, he would tell all we wished to know without any grilling.
10067{_}2138{_}I confided this idea to Godfrey as we went down the front steps.
10067{_}2139{_}"Perhaps you're right," he agreed.
10067{_}2140{_}"I don't believe the fellow is really crooked.
10067{_}2141{_}Something has happened to him--something in connection with that woman--and he has never got over it.
10067{_}2142{_}Well, we shall have to find out what it was.
10067{_}2143{_}Hello, here are Simmonds's men," he added, as two policemen stopped before the house.
10067{_}2144{_}"Is this Mr.
10067{_}2145{_}Godfrey?"
10067{_}2146{_}one of them asked.
10067{_}2147{_}"Yes," said Godfrey.
10067{_}2148{_}"Mr. Simmonds told us to report to you, sir, if you were here."

10067{_}2150{_}"Very well, sir," and the men touched their helmets, and one of them went around to the back of the house, while the other remained in front.
10067{_}2151{_}"Perhaps if they concealed themselves," I suggested, "the fellow might venture back and be nabbed."
10067{_}2152{_}But Godfrey shook his head.
10067{_}2153{_}"I don't want him to venture back," he said.
10067{_}2154{_}"I want to scare him off.
10067{_}2155{_}I want him to see we're thoroughly on guard."
10067{_}2156{_}He hailed a passing cab, and paused with one foot on the step.
10067{_}2157{_}"I've already told you, Lester," he added, over his shoulder, "that I'm afraid of him.
10067{_}2158{_}Perhaps you thought I was joking, but I wasn't.
10067{_}2159{_}I was never more serious in my life.
10067{_}2160{_}The _Record_ office," he added to the cabby, and jingled away, leaving me staring after him.
10067{_}2161{_}As I turned homeward, I could not but ponder over this remarkable and mysterious being with whom Godfrey was so impressed.
10067{_}2162{_}Never before had I known him to hesitate to match himself with any adversary; but now, it seemed to me, he shunned the contest, or at least feared it --feared that he might be outwitted and outplayed!
10067{_}2163{_}How great a compliment that was to the mysterious unknown only I could guess!
10067{_}2164{_}And then I shivered a little as I recalled that mocking and ironic laughter.
10067{_}2165{_}And I quickened my step, with a glance over my shoulder; for if Godfrey was afraid, how much more reason had I to be!
10067{_}2166{_}It was with a sense of relief, of which I was a little ashamed, that I reached my apartment at the Marathon and locked the door.
10067{_}2167{_}Just before I turned in for the night, I heard from Godfrey again, for my telephone rang, and it was his voice that answered.
10067{_}2168{_}"I just wanted to tell you, Lester," he said, "that your guess was right.
10067{_}2169{_}The mysterious Frenchman came over on _La Touraine_, landing at noon yesterday.
10067{_}2170{_}He came in the steerage, and the stewards know nothing about him.
10067{_}2171{_}What time was it he got to Vantine's?"
10067{_}2172{_}"About two, I should say."
10067{_}2173{_}"So he probably went directly there from the boat, as you thought.
10067{_}2174{_}That accounts for nobody knowing him.
10067{_}2175{_}The steamship company is holding a bag belonging to him.
10067{_}2176{_}I'll get them to open it to-morrow, and perhaps we shall find out who he was."
10067{_}2177{_}"But, Godfrey," I broke in, "how about this other fellow--the man with the burning eyes?
10067{_}2178{_}He's getting on my nerves!"
10067{_}2179{_}"Don't let him do that, Lester!"
10067{_}2180{_}he laughed.
10067{_}2181{_}"We're in no danger so long as we are not around that cabinet!
10067{_}2182{_}That's the storm centre!
10067{_}2183{_}I can't tell you more than that.
10067{_}2184{_}Good-night!"
10067{_}2185{_}and he hung up without waiting for me to answer.
10067{_}2186{_}CHAPTER XIII  A DISTINGUISHED CALLER   It was shortly after I reached the office, next morning, that the office-boy came in and handed me a card with an awed and reverent air so at variance with his usual demeanour that I glanced at the square of pasteboard in some astonishment.
10067{_}2187{_}Then, I confess, an awed and reverent feeling crept over me, also, for the card bore the name of Sereno Hornblower.
10067{_}2188{_}That name is quite unknown outside the legal profession of the three great cities of the east, New York, Boston and Philadelphia; for Sereno Hornblower has never held a public office, has never made a public speech, has never responded to a toast, has never served on a public committee, has never, so far as I know, conducted a case in court or addressed a jury--has never, in a word, figured in the newspapers in any way; and yet his income would make that of any other lawyer in the country look like thirty cents.
10067{_}2189{_}For Sereno Hornblower is the confidential attorney of most of our "best families."
10067{_}2190{_}He has held that position for years, and it is said that no case placed unreservedly in his hands ever resulted in a public scandal.
10067{_}2191{_}He accepts clients with great care; he has steadfastly refused the business of Pittsburgh millionaires, remunerative as it was certain to be; but he seems to take a sort of personal pride in keeping intact the reputations of the old families, even when their scions embark in the most outrageous escapades.
10067{_}2192{_}If you are descended from the Pilgrims or the Patroons, Mr. Hornblower will ask no further recommendation.
10067{_}2193{_}His reputation for tact and delicacy is tremendous; and yet those who have found themselves opposed to him have never been long in realising that there was a most redoubtable mailed fist under the velvet glove.
10067{_}2194{_}Altogether a remarkable man, whose memoirs would make absorbing reading, could he be persuaded to write them--which is quite beyond the bounds of possibility.
10067{_}2195{_}I had never met him either professionally or personally, and it was with some eagerness that I told the office-boy to show him in at once.
10067{_}2196{_}Sereno Hornblower did not look the part.
10067{_}2197{_}His reputation led one to expect a sort of cross between Uriah Heep and Sherlock Holmes, but there was nothing secretive or insinuating about his appearance.
10067{_}2198{_}He was a bluff and hearty man of middle age, rather heavy-set, fresh-faced and clean-shaven, and with very bright blue eyes--evidently a man with a good digestion and a comfortable conscience.
10067{_}2199{_}Had I met him on Broadway, I should have taken him for a ripe and finished comedian.
10067{_}2200{_}There was about him an air which somehow reminded me of Joseph Jefferson--perhaps it was his bright blue eyes.
10067{_}2201{_}It may have been this very appearance of bluff sincerity and honest downrightness which accounted for his success.
10067{_}2202{_}We shook hands, and he sat down and plunged at once, without an instant's hesitation, into the business which had brought him.
10067{_}2203{_}Looking back at it, understanding as I do now the delicate nature of that business, I admire more and more that bluff readiness; though the more I think of it, the more I am convinced that he had thought out definitely beforehand precisely what he was going to say.
10067{_}2204{_}The man who can carry through a carefully premeditated scene with an air of complete unpremeditation has an immense advantage.
10067{_}2205{_}"Mr. Lester," he began, "I understand that you are the administrator of the estate of the late Philip Vantine?"
10067{_}2206{_}"Our firm is," I corrected.
10067{_}2207{_}"But you, personally, have been attending to his business?"
10067{_}2208{_}"Yes."
10067{_}2209{_}"He was a collector of old furniture, I believe?"
10067{_}2210{_}"Yes."
10067{_}2211{_}"And on his last trip to Europe, from which he returned only a few days ago, he purchased of Armand & Son, of Paris, a Boule cabinet?"
10067{_}2212{_}I could not repress a start of astonishment.
10067{_}2213{_}"Are you acting for Armand & Son?"
10067{_}2214{_}I queried.
10067{_}2215{_}"Not at all.
10067{_}2216{_}I am acting for a lady whom, for the present, we will call Madame X."
10067{_}2217{_}The thought flashed through my mind that Madame X. and the mysterious Frenchwoman might be one and the same person.
10067{_}2218{_}Then I put aside the idea as absurd.
10067{_}2219{_}Sereno Hornblower would never accept such a client.
10067{_}2220{_}"Mr. Vantine did buy such a cabinet," I said.
10067{_}2221{_}"And it is in your possession?"
10067{_}2222{_}"There is at his residence a Boule cabinet which was shipped him from Paris, but, only a few hours before his death, Mr. Vantine assured me that it was not the one he had purchased."
10067{_}2223{_}"You mean that a mistake had been made in the shipment?"
10067{_}2224{_}"That is what we supposed, and a cablegram from Armand & Son has since confirmed it."
10067{_}2225{_}Mr. Hornblower pondered this for a moment.

10067{_}2227{_}he asked at last.
10067{_}2228{_}"I have no idea.
10067{_}2229{_}Perhaps it is still in Paris.
10067{_}2230{_}But I am expecting a representative of the Armands to call very soon to straighten things out."
10067{_}2231{_}Again my companion fell silent, and sat rubbing his chin absently.
10067{_}2232{_}"It is very strange," he said, finally.
10067{_}2233{_}"If the cabinet was still at Paris, one would think it would have been discovered before my client made inquiry about it."
10067{_}2234{_}"There are a good many things which are strange about this whole matter," I supplemented.

10067{_}2241{_}He nodded.

10067{_}2243{_}he asked quickly.
10067{_}2244{_}"We believe so; though as yet we have been able to prove absolutely nothing.
10067{_}2245{_}But we are guarding the cabinet very closely.
10067{_}2246{_}I should not object to your client seeing it, but I could not permit her to touch it--not, at least, without knowing why she wished to do so.
10067{_}2247{_}You will remember that you have told me nothing of why she is interested in it."
10067{_}2248{_}"I am quite ready to tell you the story, Mr. Lester," he said.
10067{_}2249{_}"It is only fair that I should do so.
10067{_}2250{_}After you have heard it, if you agree, we will take Madame X. to see the cabinet."
10067{_}2251{_}"Very well," I assented.
10067{_}2252{_}He settled back in his chair, and his face became more grave.
10067{_}2253{_}"My client," he began, "is a member of a prominent American family--a most prominent family.
10067{_}2254{_}Three years ago, she married a French nobleman.
10067{_}2255{_}You can, perhaps, guess her name, but I should prefer that neither of us utter it."
10067{_}2256{_}I nodded my agreement.
10067{_}2257{_}"This nobleman has been both prodigal and unfaithful.
10067{_}2258{_}He has scattered my client's fortune with both hands.
10067{_}2259{_}He has flaunted his mistresses in her face.
10067{_}2260{_}He has even tried to compel her to receive one of them.
