10067{_}4086{_}"I shall be at the Hotel Astor, and shall be glad to see you--shall we say at eleven o'clock?
10067{_}4087{_}I am truly sorry that I can tell you nothing to-night."
10067{_}4088{_}He shook hands with the purser, waved his hand to us, and joined Grady, who was watching these amenities with evident impatience.
10067{_}4089{_}Together they disappeared down the stair.
10067{_}4090{_}"A contrast in manners, was it not, gentlemen?"
10067{_}4091{_}asked Godfrey, looking about him.
10067{_}4092{_}"Didn't you blush for America?"
10067{_}4093{_}The men laughed, for they knew he was after Grady, and yet it was evident enough that they agreed with him.
10067{_}4094{_}"Come on, Lester," he added; "we might as well be getting back.
10067{_}4095{_}I can send the boat down again after the other boys," and he turned down the stair.
10067{_}4096{_}CHAPTER XXIV  THE SECRET OF THE CABINET   Godfrey bade me good-bye at the dock and hastened away to the office to write his story, which, I could guess, would be concerned with the manners of Americans, especially with Grady's.
10067{_}4097{_}As for me, that whiff of salt air had put an unaccustomed edge to my appetite, and I took a cab to Murray's, deciding to spend the remainder of the evening there, over a good dinner.
10067{_}4098{_}Except in a certain mood, Murray's does not appeal to me; the pseudo-Grecian temple in the corner, with water cascading down its steps, the make-believe clouds which float across the ceiling, the tables of glass lighted from beneath--all this, ordinarily, seems trivial and banal; but occasionally, in an esoteric mood, I like Murray's, and can even find something picturesque and romantic in bright gowns, and gleaming shoulders, and handsome faces seen amid these bizarre surroundings.
10067{_}4099{_}And then, of course, there is always the cooking, which leaves nothing to be desired.
10067{_}4100{_}I was in the right mood to-night for the enjoyment of the place, and I ambled through the dinner in a fashion so leisurely and trifled so long over coffee and cigarette that it was far past ten o'clock when I came out again into Forty-second Street.
10067{_}4101{_}After an instant's hesitation, I decided to walk home, and turned back toward Broadway, already filling with the after-theatre crowd.
10067{_}4102{_}Often as I have seen it, Broadway at night is still a fascinating place to me, with its blazing signs, its changing crowds, its clanging street traffic, its bright shop-windows.
10067{_}4103{_}Grady was right in saying that "gay Paree" had nothing like it; nor has any other city that I know.
10067{_}4104{_}It is, indeed, unique and thoroughly American; and I walked along it that night in the most leisurely fashion, savouring it to the full; pausing, now and then, for a glance at a shop-window, and stopping at the Hoffman House--now denuded, alas!
10067{_}4105{_}of its Bouguereau--to replenish my supply of cigarettes.
10067{_}4106{_}Reaching Madison Square, at last, I walked out under the trees, as I almost always do, to have a look at the Flatiron Building, white against the sky.
10067{_}4107{_}Then I glanced up at the Metropolitan tower, higher but far less romantic in appearance, and saw by the big illuminated clock that it was nearly half-past eleven.
10067{_}4108{_}I crossed back over Broadway, at last, and turned down Twenty-third Street in the direction of the Marathon, when, just at the corner, I came face to face with three men as they swung around the corner in the same direction, and, with a little start, I recognised Grady and Simmonds, with M. Pigot between them.
10067{_}4109{_}Evidently Grady had felt it incumbent upon himself to make good his promise in the most liberal manner, and to display the wonders of the Great White Way from end to end--the ceremony no doubt involving the introduction of the stranger to a number of typical American drinks--and the result of all this was that Grady's legs wobbled perceptibly.
10067{_}4110{_}As a matter of racial comparison, I glanced at M. Pigot's, but they seemed in every way normal.
10067{_}4111{_}"Hello, Lester," said Simmonds, in a voice which showed that he had not wholly escaped the influences of the evening's celebration; and even Grady condescended to nod, from which I inferred that he was feeling very unusually happy.
10067{_}4112{_}"Hello, Simmonds," I answered, and, as I turned westward with them, he dropped back and; fell into step beside me.
10067{_}4113{_}"Piggott is certainly a wonder," he said.
10067{_}4114{_}"A regular sport--wanted to see everything and taste everything.
10067{_}4115{_}He says Paris ain't in the same class with this town."
10067{_}4116{_}"Where are you going now?"
10067{_}4117{_}I asked.
10067{_}4118{_}"We're going round to the station.
10067{_}4119{_}Piggott says he's got a sensation up his sleeve for us--it's got something to do with that cabinet."
10067{_}4120{_}"With the cabinet?"
10067{_}4121{_}"Yes--that shiny thing Godfrey got me to lock up in a cell."
10067{_}4122{_}"Simmonds," I said, seriously, "does Godfrey know about this?"
10067{_}4123{_}"No," said Simmonds, looking a little uncomfortable.
10067{_}4124{_}"I told Grady we ought to 'phone him to come up, but the chief got mad and told me to mind my own business.
10067{_}4125{_}Godfrey's been after him, you know, for a long time."
10067{_}4126{_}"Suppose I 'phone him," I suggested.
10067{_}4127{_}"There'd be no objection to that, would there?"
10067{_}4128{_}"_I_ won't object," said Simmonds, "and I don't know who else will, since nobody else will know about it."
10067{_}4129{_}"All right.
10067{_}4130{_}And drag out the preliminaries as long as you can, to give him a chance to get up here."
10067{_}4131{_}Simmonds nodded.
10067{_}4132{_}"I'll do what I can," he agreed, "but I don't see what good it will do.
10067{_}4133{_}The chief won't let him in, even if he does come up."
10067{_}4134{_}"We'll have to leave that to Godfrey.
10067{_}4135{_}But he ought to be told.
10067{_}4136{_}He's responsible for the cabinet being where it is."
10067{_}4137{_}"I know he is, and Piggott says it was a mighty wise thing to put it there, though I'm blessed if I know why.
10067{_}4138{_}Hurry Godfrey along as much as you can.
10067{_}4139{_}Good-night," and he followed his companions into the station.
10067{_}4140{_}There was a drugstore at the corner with a public telephone station, and two minutes later, I was asking to be connected with the city-room at the _Record_ office.
10067{_}4141{_}No, said a supercilious voice, Mr. Godfrey was not there; he had left some time before; no, the speaker did not know where he was going, nor when he would be back.
10067{_}4142{_}"Look here," I said, "this is important.
10067{_}4143{_}I want to talk to the city editor--and be quick about it."
10067{_}4144{_}There was an instant's astonished silence.
10067{_}4145{_}"What name?"
10067{_}4146{_}asked the voice.
10067{_}4147{_}"Lester, of Royce and Lester--and you might tell your city editor that Godfrey is a close friend of mine."
10067{_}4148{_}The city editor seemed to understand, for I was switched on to him a moment later.
10067{_}4149{_}But he was scarcely more satisfactory.
10067{_}4150{_}"We sent Godfrey up into Westchester to see a man," he said, "on a tip that looked pretty good.
10067{_}4151{_}He started just as soon as he got his Pigot story written, and he ought to be back almost any time.
10067{_}4152{_}Is there a message I can give him?"
10067{_}4153{_}"Yes--tell him Pigot is at the Twenty-third Street station, and that he'd better come up as soon as he can."
10067{_}4154{_}"Very good.
10067{_}4155{_}I'll give him the message the moment he comes in."
10067{_}4156{_}"Thank you," I said, but the disappointment was a bitter one.
10067{_}4157{_}In the street again, I paused hesitatingly at the curb, my eyes on the red light of the police station.
10067{_}4158{_}What was about to happen there?
10067{_}4159{_}What was the sensation M. Pigot had up his sleeve?
10067{_}4160{_}Had I any excuse for being present?
10067{_}4161{_}And then, remembering Grady's nod and his wobbly legs--remembering, too, that, at the worst, he could only put me out!--I turned toward the light, pushed open the door and entered.
10067{_}4162{_}There was no one in sight except the sergeant at the desk.
10067{_}4163{_}"My name is Lester," I said.
10067{_}4164{_}"You have a cabinet here belonging to the estate of the late Philip Vantine."
10067{_}4165{_}"We've got a cabinet, all right; but I don't know who it belongs to."
10067{_}4166{_}"It belongs to Mr. Vantine's estate."
10067{_}4167{_}"Well, what about it?"
10067{_}4168{_}he asked, looking at me to see if I was drunk.
10067{_}4169{_}"You haven't come in here at midnight to tell me that, I hope?"
10067{_}4170{_}"No; but I'd like to see the cabinet a minute."
10067{_}4171{_}"You can't see it to-night.
10067{_}4172{_}Come around to-morrow.
10067{_}4173{_}Besides, I don't know you."
10067{_}4174{_}"Here's my card.
10067{_}4175{_}Either Mr. Simmonds or Mr. Grady would know me.
10067{_}4176{_}And to-morrow won't do."
10067{_}4177{_}The sergeant took the card, looked at it, and looked at me.
10067{_}4178{_}"Wait a minute," he said, at last, and disappeared through a door at the farther side of the room.
10067{_}4179{_}He was gone three or four minutes, and the station-clock struck twelve as I stood there.
10067{_}4180{_}I counted the sonorous, deliberate strokes, and then, in the silence that followed, my hands began to tremble with the suspense.
10067{_}4181{_}Suppose Grady should refuse to see me?
10067{_}4182{_}But at last the sergeant came back.
10067{_}4183{_}"Come along," he said, opening the gate in the railing and motioning me through.
10067{_}4184{_}"Straight on through that door," he added, and sat down again at his desk.
10067{_}4185{_}With a desperate effort at careless unconcern, I opened the door and passed through.
10067{_}4186{_}Then, involuntarily, I stopped.
10067{_}4187{_}For there, in the middle of the floor, was the Boule cabinet, with M. Pigot standing beside it, and Grady and Simmonds sitting opposite, flung carelessly back in their chairs, and puffing at black cigars.
10067{_}4188{_}They all looked at me as I entered, Pigot with an evident contraction of the brows which showed how strongly his urbanity was strained; Simmonds with an affectation of surprise, and Grady with a bland and somewhat vacant smile.
10067{_}4189{_}My heart rose when I saw that smile.
10067{_}4190{_}"Well, Mr. Lester," he said, "so you want to see this cabinet?"
10067{_}4191{_}"Yes," I answered; "it really belongs to the Vantine estate, you know; I'm going to put in a claim for it--that is, if you are not willing to surrender it without contest."
10067{_}4192{_}"Did you just happen to think of this in the middle of the night?"
10067{_}4193{_}he inquired quizzically.
10067{_}4194{_}"No," I said, boldly; "but I saw you and Mr. Simmonds and this gentleman"--with a bow to M. Pigot--"turn in here a moment ago, and it occurred to me that the cabinet might have something to do with your visit.
10067{_}4195{_}Of course, we don't want the cabinet injured.
10067{_}4196{_}It is very valuable."
10067{_}4197{_}"Don't worry," said Grady, easily, "we're not going to injure it.
10067{_}4198{_}And I think we'll be ready to surrender it to you at any time after to-night.
10067{_}4199{_}Moosseer Piggott here wants to do a few tricks with it first.
10067{_}4200{_}I suppose you have a certain right to be present--so, if you like sleight-of-hand, sit down."
10067{_}4201{_}I hastily sought a chair, my heart singing within me.
10067{_}4202{_}Then I attempted to assume a mask of indifference, for M. Pigot was obviously annoyed at my presence, and I feared for a moment that his Gallic suavity would be strained to breaking.
10067{_}4203{_}But Grady, if he noticed his guest's annoyance, paid no heed to it; and I began to suspect that the Frenchman's courtesy and good-breeding had ended by rubbing Grady the wrong way, they were in such painful contrast to his own hob-nailed manners.
10067{_}4204{_}Whatever the cause, there was a certain malice in the smile he turned upon the Frenchman.
10067{_}4205{_}"And now, Moosseer Piggott," he said, settling back in his chair a little farther, "we're ready for the show."
10067{_}4206{_}"What I have to tell you, sir," began M. Pigot, in a voice as hard as steel and cold as ice, "has, understand well, to be told in confidence.
10067{_}4207{_}It must remain between ourselves until the criminal is secured."
10067{_}4208{_}Grady's smile hardened a little.
10067{_}4209{_}Perhaps he did not like the imperatives.
10067{_}4210{_}At any rate, he ignored the hint.
10067{_}4211{_}"Understand, Mr.
10067{_}4212{_}Lester?"
10067{_}4213{_}he asked, looking at me, and I nodded.
10067{_}4214{_}I saw Pigot's eyes flame and his face flush with anger, for Grady's tone was almost insulting.
10067{_}4215{_}For an instant I thought that he would refuse to proceed; but he controlled himself.
10067{_}4216{_}Standing there facing me, in the full light, it was possible for me to examine him much more closely than had been possible on board the boat, and I looked at him with interest.
10067{_}4217{_}He was typically French, --smooth-shaven, with a face seamed with little wrinkles and very white, eyes shadowed by enormously bushy lashes, and close-cropped hair as white as his face.
10067{_}4218{_}But what attracted me most was the mouth --a mouth at once delicate and humourous, a little large and with the lips full enough to betoken vigour, yet not too full for fineness.
10067{_}4219{_}He was about sixty years of age, I guessed; and there was about him the air of a man who had passed through a hundred remarkable experiences, without once losing his aplomb.
10067{_}4220{_}Certainly he was not going to lose it now.
10067{_}4221{_}"The story which I have to relate," he began in his careful English, clipping his words a little now and then, "has to do with the theft of the famous Michaelovitch diamonds.
10067{_}4222{_}You may, perhaps, remember the case."
10067{_}4223{_}I remembered it, certainly, for the robbery had been conceived and carried out with such brilliancy and daring that its details had at once arrested my attention--to say nothing of the fact that the diamonds, which formed the celebrated collection belonging to the Grand Duke Michael, of Russia,--sojourning in Paris because unappreciated in his native land and also because of the supreme attraction of the French capital to one of his temperament--were valued at something like eight million francs.
10067{_}4224{_}"That theft," continued M. Pigot, "was accomplished in a manner at once so bold and so unique that we were certain it could be the work of but a single man--a rascal named Crochard, who calls himself also 'The Invincible'--a rascal who has given us very great trouble, but whom we have never been able to convict.
10067{_}4225{_}In this case, we had against him no direct evidence; we subjected him to an interrogation and found that he had taken care to provide a perfect alibi; so we were compelled to release him.
10067{_}4226{_}We knew that it would be quite useless to arrest him unless we should find some of the stolen jewels in his possession.
10067{_}4227{_}He appeared as usual upon the boulevards, at the cafes, everywhere.
10067{_}4228{_}He laughed in our faces.
10067{_}4229{_}For us, it was not pleasant; but our law is strict.
10067{_}4230{_}For us to accuse a man, to arrest him, and then to be compelled to own ourselves mistaken, is a very serious matter.
10067{_}4231{_}But we did what we could.
10067{_}4232{_}We kept Crochard under constant surveillance; we searched his rooms and those of his mistress not once but many times.
10067{_}4233{_}On one occasion, when he passed the barrier at Vincennes, our agents fell upon him and searched him, under pretence of robbing him.
10067{_}4234{_}"He was, understand well, not for an instant deceived.
10067{_}4235{_}He knew thoroughly what we were doing, for what we were searching.
10067{_}4236{_}He knew also that nowhere in Europe would he dare to attempt to sell a single one of those jewels.
10067{_}4237{_}We suspected that he would attempt to bring them to this country, and we warned your department of customs.
10067{_}4238{_}For we knew that here he could sell all but the very largest not only almost without danger, but at a price far greater than he could obtain for them in Europe.
10067{_}4239{_}We closed every avenue to him, as we thought--and then, all at once, he disappeared.
10067{_}4240{_}"For two weeks we heard nothing--then came the story of this man Drouet, killed by a stab on the hand.
10067{_}4241{_}At once we recognised the work of Crochard, for he alone of living men possesses the secret of the poison of the Medici.
10067{_}4242{_}It is a fearful secret, which, in his whole life, he had used but once--and that upon a man who had betrayed him."
10067{_}4243{_}M. Pigot paused and passed his hand across his forehead.
10067{_}4244{_}"We were at a loss to understand Crochard's connection with Drouet," M. Pigot continued.
10067{_}4245{_}"Drouet, while a mere hanger-on of the cafes of the boulevards, was not a criminal.
10067{_}4246{_}Then came the death of that creature Morel, in an effort to gain possession of this cabinet, and we began to understand.
10067{_}4247{_}We made inquiries concerning the cabinet; we learned its history, and the secret of its construction, and we arrived at a certain conclusion.
10067{_}4248{_}It was to ascertain if that conclusion is correct that I came to America."
10067{_}4249{_}"What is the conclusion?"
10067{_}4250{_}queried Grady, who had listened to all this with a manifest impatience in strong contrast to my own absorbed interest.
10067{_}4251{_}For I had already guessed what the conclusion was, and my pulses were bounding with excitement.
10067{_}4252{_}"Our theory," replied M. Pigot, without the slightest acceleration of speech, "is that the Michaelovitch diamonds are concealed in this cabinet.
10067{_}4253{_}Everything points to it--and we shall soon see."
10067{_}4254{_}As he spoke, he drew from his pocket a steel gauntlet, marvellously like the one Godfrey had used, and slipped it over his right hand.
10067{_}4255{_}"When one attempts to fathom the secrets of _L'Invincible_" he said with a smile, "one must go armoured.
10067{_}4256{_}Already three men have paid with their lives the penalty of their rashness."
10067{_}4257{_}"Three men!"
10067{_}4258{_}repeated Grady, wonderingly.
10067{_}4259{_}"Three," and Pigot checked them off upon his fingers.
10067{_}4260{_}"First the man who gave his name as d'Aurelle, but who was really a blackmailer named Drouet; second, M. Vantine, the connoisseur; and third, the creature Morel.
10067{_}4261{_}Of these, the only one that really matters is M. Vantine; his death was most unfortunate, and I am sure that Crochard regrets it exceedingly.
10067{_}4262{_}He might also regret my death, but, at any rate, I have no wish to be the fourth.
10067{_}4263{_}Not I," and he adjusted the gauntlet carefully.
10067{_}4264{_}"One moment, monsieur," I said, bursting in, unable to remain longer silent.
10067{_}4265{_}"This is all so wonderful--so thrilling--will you not tell us more?
10067{_}4266{_}For what were these three men searching?
10067{_}4267{_}For the jewels?"
10067{_}4268{_}"Monsieur is as familiar with the facts as I," he answered, in a sarcastic tone.
10067{_}4269{_}"He knows that Drouet was killed while searching for a packet of letters, which would have compromised most seriously a great lady; he knows that M. Vantine was killed while endeavouring to open the drawer after its secret had been revealed to him by the maid of that same great lady, who was hoping to get a reward for them; Morel met death directly at the hands of Crochard because he was a traitor and deserved it."
10067{_}4270{_}More and more fascinated, I stared at him.
10067{_}4271{_}What secret was safe, I asked myself, from this astonishing man?
10067{_}4272{_}Or was he merely piecing together the whole story from such fragments as he knew?
10067{_}4273{_}"But even yet," I stammered, "I do not understand.
10067{_}4274{_}We have opened the secret drawer of the cabinet--there was no poison.
10067{_}4275{_}How could it have killed Drouet and Mr.
10067{_}4276{_}Vantine?"
10067{_}4277{_}"Very simply," said M. Pigot, coldly.
10067{_}4278{_}"Death came to Drouet and M. Vantine because the maid of Madame la Duchesse mistook her left hand for her right.
10067{_}4279{_}The drawer which contained the letters is at the left of the cabinet--see," and he pressed the series of springs, caught the little handle, and pulled the drawer open.
10067{_}4280{_}"You will notice that the letters are gone, for the drawer was opened by Madame la Duchesse herself, in the presence of M. Lestaire, who very gallantly permitted her to resume possession of them.
10067{_}4281{_}The drawer which Drouet and M. Vantine opened," and here his voice became a little strident under the stress of great emotion, "is on the right side of the cabinet, exactly opposite the other, and opened by a similar combination.
10067{_}4282{_}But there is one great difference.
10067{_}4283{_}About the first drawer, there is nothing to harm any one; the other is guarded by the deadliest poison the world has ever known.
10067{_}4284{_}Observe me, gentlemen!"
10067{_}4285{_}Impelled by an excitement so intense as to be almost painful, I had risen from my chair and drawn near to him.
10067{_}4286{_}As he spoke, he bent above the desk and pressed three fingers along the right edge.
10067{_}4287{_}There was a sharp click, and a section of the inlay fell outward, forming a handle, just as I had seen it do on the other side of the desk.
10067{_}4288{_}M. Pigot hesitated an instant--any man would have hesitated before that awful risk!--then, catching the handle firmly with his armoured hand, he drew it quickly out.
10067{_}4289{_}There was a sharp clash, as of steel on steel, and the drawer stood open.
10067{_}4290{_}CHAPTER XXV  THE MICHAELOVITCH DIAMONDS   M. Pigot, cool and imperturbable, held out to us, with a little smile, a hand which showed not a quiver of emotion--his gauntleted hand; and I saw that, on the back of it, were two tiny depressions.
10067{_}4291{_}At the bottom of each depression lay a drop of bright red liquid-- blood-red, I told myself, as I stared at it, fascinated.
10067{_}4292{_}And what nerves of steel this man possessed!
10067{_}4293{_}A sudden warmth of admiration for him glowed within me.
10067{_}4294{_}"That liquid, gentlemen," he said in his smooth voice, "is the most powerful poison ever distilled by man.
10067{_}4295{_}Those two tiny drops would kill a score of people, and kill them instantly.
10067{_}4296{_}Its odour betrays its origin"--and, indeed, the air was heavy with the scent of bitter almonds--"but the poison ordinarily derived from that source is as nothing compared with this.
10067{_}4297{_}This poison is said to have been discovered by Remy, the remarkable man who brought about the death of the Duc d'Anjou.
10067{_}4298{_}Its distillation was supposed to be one of the lost arts, but the secret was rediscovered by this man Crochard.
10067{_}4299{_}No secret, indeed, is safe from him; criminal history, criminal memoirs--the mysteries and achievements of the great confederacy of crime which has existed for many centuries, and whose existence few persons even suspect--all this is to him an open book.
10067{_}4300{_}It is this which renders him so formidable.
10067{_}4301{_}No man can stand against him.
10067{_}4302{_}Even the secret of this drawer was known to him, and he availed himself of it when need arose."
10067{_}4303{_}M. Pigot paused, his head bent in thought; and I seemed to be gazing with him down long avenues of crime, extending far into the past--dismal avenues like those of Pere Lachaise, where tombs elbowed each other; where, at every step, one came face to face with a mystery, a secret, or a tragedy.
10067{_}4304{_}Only, here, the mysteries were all solved, the secrets all uncovered, the tragedies all understood.
10067{_}4305{_}But only to the elect, to criminals really great, were these avenues open; to all others they were forbidden.
10067{_}4306{_}Alone of living men, perhaps, Crochard was free to wander there unchallenged.
10067{_}4307{_}Some such vision as this, I say, passed before my eyes, and I had a feeling that M. Pigot shared in it; but, after an instant, he turned back to the cabinet.
10067{_}4308{_}"Now, M. Simmon," he said, briskly, in an altered voice, "if you will have the kindness to hold the drawer for a moment in this position, I will draw the serpent's fangs.
10067{_}4309{_}There is not the slightest danger," he added, seeing that Simmonds very naturally hesitated.
10067{_}4310{_}Thus assured, Simmonds grasped the handle of the drawer, and held it open, while the Frenchman took from his pocket a tiny flask of crystal.
10067{_}4311{_}"A little farther," he said; and as Simmonds, with evident effort, drew the drawer out to its full length, a tiny, two-tined prong pushed itself forward from underneath the cabinet.
10067{_}4312{_}"There are the fangs," said M. Pigot.
10067{_}4313{_}He held the mouth of the flask under first one and then the other, passing his other hand carefully behind and above them.
10067{_}4314{_}"The poison is held in place by what we in French call _attraction capillaire_--I do not know the English; but I drive it out by introducing the air behind it--ah, you see!"
10067{_}4315{_}He stood erect and held the flask up to the light.
10067{_}4316{_}It was half full of the red liquid.
10067{_}4317{_}"Enough to decimate France," he said, screwed the stopper carefully into place, and put the flask in his pocket.
10067{_}4318{_}"Release the drawer, if you please, monsieur," he added to Simmonds.
10067{_}4319{_}It sprang back into place on the instant, the arabesqued handle snapping up with a little click.
10067{_}4320{_}"You will observe its ingenuity," said M. Pigot.
10067{_}4321{_}"It is really most clever.
10067{_}4322{_}For whenever the hand, struck by the poisoned fangs, loosened its hold on the drawer, the drawer sprang shut as you see, and everything was as before--except that one man more had tasted death.
10067{_}4323{_}Now I open it.
10067{_}4324{_}The fangs fall again; they strike the gauntlet; but for that, they would pierce the hand, but death no longer follows.
10067{_}4325{_}By turning this button, I lock the spring, and the drawer remains open.
10067{_}4326{_}The man who devised this mechanism was so proud of it that he described it in a secret memoir for the entertainment of the Grand Louis.
10067{_}4327{_}There is a copy of that memoir among the archives of the Bibliotheque Nationale; the original is owned by Crochard.
10067{_}4328{_}It was he who connected that memoir with this cabinet, who rediscovered the mechanism, rewound the spring, and renewed the poison.
10067{_}4329{_}No doubt the stroke with the poisoned fangs, which he used to punish traitors, was the result of reading that memoir."
10067{_}4330{_}"This Croshar--or whatever his name is,--seems to be a 'strordinary feller," observed Grady, relighting his cigar.
10067{_}4331{_}"He is," agreed M. Pigot, quietly; "a most extraordinary man.
10067{_}4332{_}But even he is not infallible; for, since the memoir made no mention of the other secret drawer--the one in which Madame la Duchesse concealed her love letters--Crochard knew nothing of it.
10067{_}4333{_}It was that fact which defeated his combinations--a pure accident which he could not foresee.
10067{_}4334{_}And now, gentlemen, it shall be my pleasure to display before you some very beautiful brilliants."
10067{_}4335{_}Not until that instant had I thought of what the drawer contained; I had been too fascinated by the poisoned fangs and by the story told so quietly but so effectively by the French detective; but now I perceived that the drawer was filled with little rolls of cotton, which had been pressed into it quite tightly.
10067{_}4336{_}M. Pigot removed the first of these, unrolled it and spread it out upon the desk, and instantly we caught the glitter of diamonds --diamonds so large, so brilliant, so faultlessly white that I drew a deep breath of admiration.
10067{_}4337{_}Even M. Pigot, evidently as he prided himself upon his imperturbability, could not look upon those gems wholly unmoved; a slow colour crept into his cheeks as he gazed down at them, and he picked up one or two of the larger ones to admire them more closely.
10067{_}4338{_}Then he unfolded roll after roll, stopping from time to time for a look at the larger brilliants.
10067{_}4339{_}"These are from the famous necklace which the Grand Duke inherited from his grandmother," he said, calling our attention to a little pile of marvellous gems in one of the last packets.
10067{_}4340{_}"Crochard, of course, removed them from their settings--that was inevitable.
10067{_}4341{_}He could melt down the settings and sell the gold; but not one of these brilliants would be marketable in Europe for many years.
10067{_}4342{_}Each of them is a marked gem.
10067{_}4343{_}Here in America, your police regulations are not so complete; but I fancy that, even here, he would have had difficulty in marketing this one," and he unfolded the last packet, and held up to the light a rose-diamond which seemed to me as large as a walnut, and a-glow with lovely colour.
10067{_}4344{_}"Perhaps you have stopped to admire the Mazarin diamond in the _galerie d'Apollon_ at the Louvre," said M. Pigot.
10067{_}4345{_}"There is always a crowd about that case, and a special attendant is installed there to guard it, for it contains some articles of great value.
10067{_}4346{_}But the Mazarin is not one of them; for it is not a diamond at all; it is paste--a paste facsimile of which this is the original.
10067{_}4347{_}Oh, it is all quite honest," he added, as Grady snorted derisively.
10067{_}4348{_}"Some years ago, the directors of the Louvre needed a fund for the purchase of new paintings; needed also to clean and restore the old ones.
10067{_}4349{_}They decided that it was folly to keep three millions of francs imprisoned in a single gem, when their Michael Angelos and da Vincis and Murillos were encrusted with dirt and fading daily.
10067{_}4350{_}So they sought a purchaser for the Mazarin; they found one in the empress of Russia, who had a craze for precious stones, and who, at her death, left this remarkable collection to her favourite son, who had inherited her passion.
10067{_}4351{_}A paste replica of the Mazarin was placed in the Louvre for the crowds to admire, and every one soon forgot that it was not really the diamond.
10067{_}4352{_}For myself, I think the directors acted most wisely.
10067{_}4353{_}And now," he added, with a gesture toward the glittering heaps, "what shall we do with all this?"
10067{_}4354{_}"There's only one thing to do," said Grady, awaking suddenly as from a trance, "and that's to get them in a safe-deposit box as quick as possible.
10067{_}4355{_}There's no police-safe I'd trust with 'em!
10067{_}4356{_}Why, they'd tempt the angel Gabriel!"
10067{_}4357{_}and he drew a deep breath.
10067{_}4358{_}"Can we find a box of safe-deposit at this hour of the night?"
10067{_}4359{_}asked M. Pigot, glancing at his watch.
10067{_}4360{_}"It is almost one o'clock and a half."
10067{_}4361{_}"That's easy in New York," said Grady.
10067{_}4362{_}"We'll take 'em over to the Day and Night Bank on Fifth Avenue.
10067{_}4363{_}It never closes.
10067{_}4364{_}Wait till I get something to put 'em in."
10067{_}4365{_}He went out and came back presently with a small valise.
10067{_}4366{_}"This will do," he said.
10067{_}4367{_}"Stow 'em away, and I'll call up the bank and arrange for the box."
10067{_}4368{_}Simmonds and Pigot rolled up the packets carefully and placed them in the valise, while I sat watching them in a kind of daze.
10067{_}4369{_}And I understood the temptation which would assail a man in the presence of so much beauty.
10067{_}4370{_}It was not the value of the jewels which shook and dazzled me--I scarcely thought of that; it was their seductive brilliance, it was the thought that, if I possessed them, I might take them out at any hour of the day or night and run my fingers through them and watch them shimmer and quiver in the light.
10067{_}4371{_}"The Grand Duke Michael must have been considerably upset," remarked Simmonds, who, throughout all this scene, had lost no whit of his serenity of demeanour.
10067{_}4372{_}"He has been like a madman," said M. Pigot, smiling a little at Simmonds's unemotional tone.
10067{_}4373{_}"These jewels are a passion with him; he worships them; he never has parted with them, even for a day; where he goes, they have gone.
10067{_}4374{_}In his most desperate need of money--and he has had such need many times--he has never sold one of his brilliants.
10067{_}4375{_}On the contrary, whenever he has money or credit, and the opportunity comes to purchase a stone of unusual beauty, he cannot resist, even though his debts go unpaid.
10067{_}4376{_}Since the loss of these stones, he has raved, he has cursed, he has beat his servants--one of them has died, in consequence.
10067{_}4377{_}We are all a little mad on some one subject, I have heard it said; well, the Grand Duke Michael is very mad on the subject of diamonds."
10067{_}4378{_}"Why didn't he offer a reward for their return?"
10067{_}4379{_}queried Simmonds.
10067{_}4380{_}"Oh, he did," said M. Pigot.
10067{_}4381{_}"He offered immediately his whole fortune for their return.
10067{_}4382{_}But his fortune was not large enough to tempt Crochard, for the Grand Duke really has nothing but the income from his family estates, and you may well believe that he spends all of it.
10067{_}4383{_}It will be a great joy to him that we have found them."
10067{_}4384{_}The thought flashed through my mind that doubtless M. Pigot was in the way of receiving a handsome present.
10067{_}4385{_}"There they are," said Simmonds, and closed the bag with a snap, as Grady came in again.
10067{_}4386{_}"I've arranged for the box," said Grady, "and one of our wagons is at the door.
10067{_}4387{_}I thought we'd better not trust a taxi--might turn over or run into something, and we can't afford to take any chances--not this trip.
10067{_}4388{_}Simmonds, you go along with Moosseer Piggott, and put an extra man on the seat with the driver.
10067{_}4389{_}Maybe that Croshar might try to hold you up."
10067{_}4390{_}The same thought was in my own mind, for Crochard must have learned of M. Pigot's arrival; and I could scarcely imagine that he would sit quietly by and permit the jewels to be taken away from him--to say nothing of his chagrin over his unfulfilled boast to Godfrey.
10067{_}4391{_}So I was relieved that Grady was wise enough to take no risk.
10067{_}4392{_}"You'd better get a receipt," Grady went on, "and arrange that the valise is to be delivered only when you and Moosseer Piggott appear together.
10067{_}4393{_}That will be satisfactory, moosseer?"
10067{_}4394{_}he added, turning to the Frenchman.
10067{_}4395{_}"Entirely so, sir."
10067{_}4396{_}"Very well, then; I'll see you in the morning.
10067{_}4397{_}I congratulate you on the find.
10067{_}4398{_}It was certainly great work."
10067{_}4399{_}"I thank you, sir," replied M. Pigot, gravely.
10067{_}4400{_}"Au revoir, monsieur," and with a bow to me, he followed Simmonds into the outer room.
10067{_}4401{_}Grady sat down and got out a fresh cigar.
10067{_}4402{_}"Well, Mr. Lester," he said, as he struck a match, "what do you think of these Frenchmen, anyway?"
10067{_}4403{_}"They're marvellous," I said.
10067{_}4404{_}"Even yet I can't understand how he knew so much."
10067{_}4405{_}"Maybe he was just guessing at some of it," Grady suggested.
10067{_}4406{_}"I thought of that; but I don't believe anybody could guess so accurately.
10067{_}4407{_}For instance, how did he know about those letters?"
10067{_}4408{_}"Fact is," broke in Grady, "that's the first I'd heard of 'em.
10067{_}4409{_}What _is_ that story?"
10067{_}4410{_}I told him the story briefly, carefully suppressing everything which would give him a clue to the identity of the veiled lady.
10067{_}4411{_}"There were certain details," I added, "which I supposed were known to no one except myself and two other persons--and yet M. Pigot knew them.
10067{_}4412{_}Then again, how did he know so certainly just how the mechanism worked?
10067{_}4413{_}How did he know which roll of cotton contained that Mazarin diamond?
10067{_}4414{_}You will remember he told us what was in that roll before he opened it."
10067{_}4415{_}Grady smiled good-naturedly and a little patronisingly.
10067{_}4416{_}"That was the last roll, wasn't it?"
10067{_}4417{_}he demanded.
10067{_}4418{_}"Since that big diamond hadn't shown up in any of the others, he knew it had to be in that roll.
10067{_}4419{_}It was just one of the little plays for effect them Frenchies are so fond of."
10067{_}4420{_}"Perhaps you are right," I agreed.
10067{_}4421{_}"But it seemed to me that he handled that mechanism as though he was familiar with it.
10067{_}4422{_}Of course, he may have prepared himself by studying the drawings which no doubt accompany the secret memoir.
10067{_}4423{_}He may even have had a working model made."
10067{_}4424{_}Grady nodded tolerantly.
10067{_}4425{_}"Them fellers go to a lot of trouble over little things like that," he said.
10067{_}4426{_}"They like to slam their cards down on the table with a big hurrah, even when the cards ain't worth a damn."
10067{_}4427{_}"He certainly held trumps this time, anyway," I commented.
10067{_}4428{_}"And he played his hand superbly.
10067{_}4429{_}He is an extraordinary man."
10067{_}4430{_}"And a great actor," Grady supplemented.
10067{_}4431{_}"Them fellers always behave like they was on the stage, right in the spot-light.
10067{_}4432{_}It makes me a little tired, sometimes.
10067{_}4433{_}Hello!
10067{_}4434{_}Who's that?"
10067{_}4435{_}The front door had been flung open; there was an instant's colloquy with the desk-sergeant, then a rapid step crossed the outer room, and Godfrey burst in upon us.
10067{_}4436{_}He cast a rapid glance at the Boule cabinet, at the secret drawer standing open, empty; and then his eyes rested upon Grady.
10067{_}4437{_}"So he got away with it, did he?"
10067{_}4438{_}he inquired.
10067{_}4439{_}"Who in hell do you think you are?"
10067{_}4440{_}shouted Grady, his face purple, "coming in here like this?
10067{_}4441{_}Get out, or I'll have you thrown out!"
10067{_}4442{_}"Oh, I'll go," retorted Godfrey coolly.
10067{_}4443{_}"I've seen all I care to see.
10067{_}4444{_}Only I'll tell you one thing, Grady--you've signed your own death-warrant to-night!"
10067{_}4445{_}"What do you mean by that?"
10067{_}4446{_}Grady demanded, in a lower tone.
10067{_}4447{_}"I mean that you won't last an hour after the story of this night's work gets out."
10067{_}4448{_}Grady's colour slowly faded as he met the burning and contemptuous gaze Godfrey turned upon him.
10067{_}4449{_}As for me, an awful fear had gripped my heart.
10067{_}4450{_}"Do you mean to say it wasn't Piggott?"
10067{_}4451{_}stammered Grady, at last.
10067{_}4452{_}Godfrey laughed scornfully.
10067{_}4453{_}"No, you blithering idiot!"
10067{_}4454{_}he said.
10067{_}4455{_}"It wasn't Pigot.
10067{_}4456{_}It was Crochard himself!"
10067{_}4457{_}And he stalked out, slamming the door behind him.
10067{_}4458{_}CHAPTER XXVI  THE FATE OF M. PIGOT   Whatever may have been Grady's defects of insight and imagination, he was energetic enough when thoroughly aroused.
10067{_}4459{_}Almost before the echo of that slamming door had died away, he was beside the sergeant's desk.
10067{_}4460{_}"Get out the reserves," he ordered, "and have the other wagon around.
10067{_}4461{_}'Phone headquarters to rush every man available up to the Day and Night Bank, and say it's from me!"
10067{_}4462{_}He stood chewing his cigar savagely as the sergeant hastened to obey.
10067{_}4463{_}In a moment, the reserves came tumbling out, struggling into their coats; there was a clatter of hoofs in the street as the wagon dashed up; the reserves piled into it, permitting me to crowd in beside them, Grady jumped to the seat beside the driver, and we were off at a gallop, our gong waking the echoes of the silent street.
10067{_}4464{_}I clung to the hand-rail as the wagon swayed back and forth or bounded into the air as it struck the car-tracks, and stared out into the night, struggling to understand.
10067{_}4465{_}Could Godfrey be right?
10067{_}4466{_}But of course he was right!
10067{_}4467{_}Some intuition told me that; and yet, how had Crochard managed to substitute himself for the French detective?
10067{_}4468{_}Where was Pigot?
10067{_}4469{_}Was he lying somewhere in a crumpled heap, with a tiny wound upon his hand?
10067{_}4470{_}But that could not be--Grady and Simmonds had been with him all the evening!
10067{_}4471{_}And could that aged Frenchman with the white, fine, wrinkled skin be also the bronzed and virile personage whom I had known as Felix Armand?
10067{_}4472{_}My reason reeled before the seeming impossibility of it--and yet, somehow, I knew that Godfrey was right!
10067{_}4473{_}The wagon came to a stop so suddenly that I was thrown violently against the man next to me, and the reserves, leaping out, swept me before them.
10067{_}4474{_}We were in front of the Day and Night Bank, and at a word from Grady, the men spread into a close cordon before the building.
10067{_}4475{_}Another police wagon stood at the curb, with the driver still on the seat, but as Grady started toward it, a figure appeared at the door of the bank and shouted to us--shouted in inarticulate words which I could not understand.
10067{_}4476{_}But Grady seemed to understand them, and went up the steps two at a time, with an agility surprising in so large a man, and which I was hard put to it to match.
10067{_}4477{_}A little group stood at one side of the vestibule looking down at some one extended on a cushioned seat.
10067{_}4478{_}And, an instant later, I saw that it was Simmonds, lying on his back, his eyes open and staring apparently at the ceiling.
10067{_}4479{_}But, at the second glance, I saw that the eyes were sightless.
10067{_}4480{_}Grady elbowed his way savagely through the group.
10067{_}4481{_}"Where's Kelly?"
10067{_}4482{_}he demanded.
10067{_}4483{_}At the words, a white-faced man in uniform arose from a chair into which he had plainly dropped exhausted.
10067{_}4484{_}"Oh, there you are!"
10067{_}4485{_}and Grady glowered at him ferociously.
10067{_}4486{_}"Now tell me what happened--and tell it quick!"
10067{_}4487{_}"Why, sir," stammered Kelly, "there wasn't anything happened.
10067{_}4488{_}Only when we stopped out there at the curb and I got down and opened the door, there wasn't nobody in the wagon but Mr. Simmonds.
10067{_}4489{_}I spoke to him and he didn't answer--and then I touched him and he kind of fell over--and then I rushed in here and 'phoned the station; but they said you'd already started for the bank; and then we went out and brought him in here--and that's all I know, sir."
10067{_}4490{_}"You didn't hear anything--no sound of a struggle?"
10067{_}4491{_}"Not a sound, sir; not a single sound."
10067{_}4492{_}"And you haven't any idea where the other man got out?"
10067{_}4493{_}"No, sir."
10067{_}4494{_}"Mr. Simmonds had a little valise with him--did you notice it?"
10067{_}4495{_}"Yes, sir; and I looked for it in the wagon, but it ain't there."
10067{_}4496{_}Grady turned away with a curse as four or five men ran in from the street--the men from headquarters, I told myself.
10067{_}4497{_}I could hear him talking to them in sharp, low tones, and then they departed as suddenly as they had come.
10067{_}4498{_}The reserves also hurried away, and I concluded that Grady was trying to throw a net about the territory in which the fugitive was probably concealed; but my interest in that manoeuvre was overshadowed, for the time being, by my anxiety for Simmonds.
10067{_}4499{_}I picked up his right hand and looked at it; then I drew a deep breath of relief, for it was uninjured.
10067{_}4500{_}"Has anyone sent for a doctor?"
10067{_}4501{_}I asked.
10067{_}4502{_}"Yes, sir," one of the bank attaches answered.
10067{_}4503{_}"We telephoned for one at once--here he is, now!"
10067{_}4504{_}he added, as a little black-bearded man entered, carry the inevitably-identifying medicine case.
10067{_}4505{_}The newcomer glanced at the body, waved us back, fell on one knee, stripped away the clothing from the breast and applied his ear to the heart.
10067{_}4506{_}Then he looked into the staring eyes, drew down the lids, watched them snap up again, and then hastily opened his case.
10067{_}4507{_}"Let's have some water," he said.
10067{_}4508{_}"Then he's not dead?"
10067{_}4509{_}I questioned, as one of the clerks sprang to obey.
10067{_}4510{_}"Dead?
10067{_}4511{_}No; but he's had a taste or whiff of something that has stopped the heart action."
10067{_}4512{_}With a queer, creepy feeling over my scalp, I remembered the little flask half-full of blood-red liquid which Crochard carried in his pocket.
10067{_}4513{_}But he had not meant murder this time; I remembered that Godfrey had said he never killed an adversary.
10067{_}4514{_}The doctor worked briskly away, and, at the end of a few minutes, Simmonds's eyes suddenly closed, he drew a long breath, and sat erect.
10067{_}4515{_}Then his eyes opened, and he sat swaying unsteadily and staring amazedly about him.
10067{_}4516{_}"Best lie down again," said the doctor soothingly.
10067{_}4517{_}"You're a little wobbly yet, you know."
10067{_}4518{_}"Where am I?"
10067{_}4519{_}gasped Simmonds.
10067{_}4520{_}Then his eyes encountered mine.
10067{_}4521{_}"Lester!"
10067{_}4522{_}he said.
10067{_}4523{_}"Where is he--Piggott?
10067{_}4524{_}Not...."  He stopped short, looked once around at the gleaming marble of the bank, fumbled for something at his side, and fell senseless on the seat.
10067{_}4525{_}I have no recollection of how I got back to the Marathon.
10067{_}4526{_}I suppose I must have walked; but my first distinct remembrance is of finding myself sitting in my favourite chair, pipe in hand.
10067{_}4527{_}The pipe was lit, so I suppose I must have lighted it mechanically, and I found that I had also mechanically changed into my lounging-coat.
10067{_}4528{_}I glanced at my watch and saw that it was nearly four o'clock.
10067{_}4529{_}The top of my head was burning as though with fever, and I went into the bathroom and turned the cold water on it.
10067{_}4530{_}The shock did me a world of good, and by the time I had finished a vigorous toweling I felt immensely better.
10067{_}4531{_}So I returned to my chair and sat down to review the events of the evening; but I found that somehow my brain refused to work, and black circles began to whirl before my eyes again.
10067{_}4532{_}"I told Godfrey I couldn't stand any more of this," I muttered, and stumbled into my bedroom, undressed with difficulty, and turned out the light.
10067{_}4533{_}Then, as I lay there, staring up into the darkness, a stinging thought brought me upright.
10067{_}4534{_}Godfrey--where was Godfrey?
10067{_}4535{_}Was he on the track of Crochard?
10067{_}4536{_}Was he daring a contest with him?
10067{_}4537{_}Perhaps, even at this moment....  Scarcely knowing what I did, I groped my way to the telephone and asked for Godfrey's number--hoping against hope absurdly--and at last, to my intense surprise and relief, I heard his voice--not a very amiable voice....
10067{_}4538{_}"Hello!"
10067{_}4539{_}he said.
10067{_}4540{_}"Godfrey," I began, "it's Lester.
10067{_}4541{_}He got away."
10067{_}4542{_}"Of course he got away.
10067{_}4543{_}You didn't call me out of bed to tell me that, I hope?"
10067{_}4544{_}"Then you knew about it?"
10067{_}4545{_}"I knew he'd get away."
10067{_}4546{_}"When the wagon got to the bank there was nobody inside but Simmonds.
10067{_}4547{_}Simmonds went along, you know."
10067{_}4548{_}"Was he hurt?"
10067{_}4549{_}"He was unconscious, but he came around all right."
10067{_}4550{_}"That's good--but Crochard wouldn't hurt him.
10067{_}4551{_}He got away with the jewels, of course?"
10067{_}4552{_}"Of course," I assented, surprised that Godfrey should take it so coolly.
10067{_}4553{_}"When you rushed out that way," I added, "I thought maybe you were going after him."
10067{_}4554{_}"With him twenty minutes in the lead?
10067{_}4555{_}I'm no such fool!
10067{_}4556{_}He got away from me the other day with a start of about half a second."
10067{_}4557{_}"I tried to get you," I explained, "as soon as Simmonds told me they were going to look at the cabinet.
10067{_}4558{_}I 'phoned the office.
10067{_}4559{_}The city editor said he had sent you out into Westchester."
10067{_}4560{_}Godfrey laughed shortly.
10067{_}4561{_}"It was a wild-goose chase," he said, "cooked up by our friend Crochard.
10067{_}4562{_}But even then, I'd have got back, if we hadn't punctured a tire when we were five miles from anywhere.
10067{_}4563{_}I knew what was up--but there I was.
10067{_}4564{_}Oh, he's made fools of us all, Lester.
10067{_}4565{_}I told you he would!"
10067{_}4566{_}"Then you didn't get my message?"
10067{_}4567{_}"Yes--they gave it to me when I 'phoned in that the Westchester business was a fake.
10067{_}4568{_}I rushed for the station, though I knew I'd be too late."
10067{_}4569{_}"But, Godfrey," I said, "I can't understand, even yet, how he did it.
10067{_}4570{_}Grady and Simmonds left the boat with Pigot and were with him all evening, showing him the sights.
10067{_}4571{_}How did Crochard get into it?
10067{_}4572{_}What did he do with Pigot?
10067{_}4573{_}Where _is_ Pigot?"
10067{_}4574{_}"He's on the _Savoie._ I rushed a wireless down to her as soon as I left the station.
10067{_}4575{_}They made a search and found Pigot bound and gagged under the berth in his stateroom."
10067{_}4576{_}I could only gasp.
10067{_}4577{_}"And to think I didn't suspect!"
10067{_}4578{_}added Godfrey, bitterly.
10067{_}4579{_}"We stood there and saw that yacht with the French flag walk away from us; we saw her put a man aboard the _Savoie_; we saw that man talking to Pigot...."  "Yes," I said, breathlessly; "yes."
10067{_}4580{_}"Well, that man was Crochard.
10067{_}4581{_}He got Pigot into his stateroom--gave him a whiff of the same stuff he used on Simmonds, no doubt; put him out of the way under the berth; got into his clothes, made up his face, _put_ on a wig--and all that while we were kicking our heels outside waiting for him."
10067{_}4582{_}"But it was a tremendous risk," I said.
10067{_}4583{_}"There were so many people on board who knew Pigot--it would have to be a perfect disguise."
10067{_}4584{_}"Crochard wouldn't stop for that.
10067{_}4585{_}But it wasn't much of a risk.
10067{_}4586{_}None of us had seen Pigot closely; all we had seen of him was the back of his head; and the passengers were all on deck watching the quarantine men.
10067{_}4587{_}And yet, of course, the disguise was a perfect one.
10067{_}4588{_}Crochard is an artist in that line, and he was, no doubt, thoroughly familiar with Pigot's appearance.
10067{_}4589{_}He deceived the purser--but the purser wouldn't suspect anything!"
10067{_}4590{_}"So it was really Crochard...."  "But _we_ ought to have suspected.
10067{_}4591{_}We ought to have suspected everything, questioned everything; I ought to have looked up that visitor and found out what became of him.
10067{_}4592{_}Instead of which, Crochard put Pigot's papers in his pocket, set his bag outside the stateroom door, and then came out calmly to meet his dear friends of the press; and I stood there talking to him like a little schoolboy--no wonder he thinks I'm a fool!"
10067{_}4593{_}"But nobody would have suspected!"
10067{_}4594{_}I gasped.
10067{_}4595{_}"Why, that man is- is...."  "A genius," said Godfrey.
10067{_}4596{_}"An absolute and unquestioned genius.
10067{_}4597{_}But I knew that all the time, and I ought to have been on guard.
10067{_}4598{_}You remember he said he would come to-day?"
10067{_}4599{_}"Yes."
10067{_}4600{_}"And you didn't believe it."
10067{_}4601{_}"I can't believe it yet."
10067{_}4602{_}"There's one consolation--it will break Grady."
10067{_}4603{_}"But, Godfrey," I said, "if you could have seen those diamonds--those beautiful diamonds--and to think he should be able to get away with them from right under our noses!"
10067{_}4604{_}"It's pretty bad, isn't it?
10067{_}4605{_}But there's no use crying over spilt milk.
10067{_}4606{_}Lester," he added, in another tone, "I want you to be in your office at noon to-morrow--or rather, to-day."
10067{_}4607{_}"All right," I promised; "I'll be there."
10067{_}4608{_}"Don't fail me.
10067{_}4609{_}There is one act of the comedy still to be played."
10067{_}4610{_}"I'll be there," I said again.
10067{_}4611{_}"But I'm afraid the last act will be an anti-climax.
10067{_}4612{_}Look here, Godfrey...."  "Now go to bed," he broke in; "you're talking like a somnambulist.
10067{_}4613{_}Get some sleep.
10067{_}4614{_}Have you arranged for that vacation?"
10067{_}4615{_}"Godfrey," I said, "tell me...."  "I won't tell you anything.
10067{_}4616{_}Only I've got one more bomb to explode, Lester, and it's a big one.
10067{_}4617{_}It will make you jump!"
10067{_}4618{_}I could hear him chuckling to himself.
10067{_}4619{_}"Good-night," he said, and hung up.
10067{_}4620{_}CHAPTER XXVII  THE LAST ACT OF THE DRAMA   I overslept, next morning, so outrageously that it was not until I had got a seat in a subway express that I had time to open my paper.
10067{_}4621{_}My first glance was for the big head that would tell of the diamond robbery; and then I realised that no morning paper would have a word of it.
10067{_}4622{_}For the robbery was only a few hours old--and yet, it seemed to me an age had passed since that moment when Godfrey had rushed in upon Grady and me.
10067{_}4623{_}So the city moved on, as yet blissfully unconscious of the sensation which would be sprung with the first afternoon editions, and over which reporters and artists and photographers were even now, no doubt, labouring.
10067{_}4624{_}I promised myself a happy half hour in reading Godfrey's story!
10067{_}4625{_}It was then that I remembered the appointment for twelve o'clock.
10067{_}4626{_}The last act of the drama was yet to be staged, Godfrey had said, and he had also spoken of a bomb--a big one!
10067{_}4627{_}I wondered what it could be, One thing was certain: if Godfrey had prepared it, its explosion would be startling enough!
10067{_}4628{_}There were a number of things at the office demanding my attention, and I was so late in getting there and the morning passed so rapidly that when the office-boy came in and announced that Mr. Grady and Mr. Simmonds were outside and wished to see me, I did not, for a moment, connect their visit with Godfrey.
10067{_}4629{_}Then I looked at my watch, saw that it was five minutes to twelve, and realised that the actors were assembling.
10067{_}4630{_}"Show them in," I said, and they entered together a minute later.
10067{_}4631{_}Grady was evidently much perturbed.
10067{_}4632{_}His usually florid face was drawn and haggard, his cheeks hung in ugly lines, there were dark pouches under his eyes, and the eyes themselves were blood-shot.
10067{_}4633{_}I guessed that he had not been to bed; that he had spent the night searching for Crochard--and it was easy enough to see that the search had been unsuccessful.
10067{_}4634{_}Simmonds, too, was looking rather shaky, and no doubt still felt the after-effects of that whiff of poison.
10067{_}4635{_}"I'm glad to see you are better, Simmonds," I said, shaking hands with him.
10067{_}4636{_}"That was a close call."
10067{_}4637{_}"It certainly was," Simmonds agreed, sinking into a chair.
10067{_}4638{_}"If I had got a little more of it, I'd never have waked up."
10067{_}4639{_}"Do you remember anything about it?"
10067{_}4640{_}"Not a thing.
10067{_}4641{_}One minute we were sitting there talking together as nice as you please--and the next thing I knew was when I woke up in the bank."
10067{_}4642{_}"Where's that man Godfrey?"
10067{_}4643{_}broke in Grady.
10067{_}4644{_}"He said he'd be here at noon," I said, and glanced at my watch.
10067{_}4645{_}"It's noon now.
10067{_}4646{_}Were you to meet him here?"
10067{_}4647{_}Grady glanced at me suspiciously.
10067{_}4648{_}"Don't you know nothing about it?"
10067{_}4649{_}he asked.
10067{_}4650{_}"I only know that Godfrey asked me to be here at noon to-day.
10067{_}4651{_}What's up?"
10067{_}4652{_}"Blamed if I know," said Grady sulkily.
10067{_}4653{_}"I got word from him that I'd better be here, and I thought maybe he might know something.
10067{_}4654{_}I'm so dizzy over last night's business that I'm running around in circles this morning.
10067{_}4655{_}But I won't wait for him.
10067{_}4656{_}He can't make me do that!
10067{_}4657{_}Come along, Simmonds."
10067{_}4658{_}"Wait a minute," I broke in, as the outer door opened.
10067{_}4659{_}"Perhaps that's Godfrey, now."
10067{_}4660{_}And so it proved.
10067{_}4661{_}He came in accompanied by a man whom I knew to be Arthur Shearrow, chief counsel for the _Record_.
10067{_}4662{_}Godfrey nodded all around.
10067{_}4663{_}"I think you know Mr. Shearrow," he said, placing on my desk a small leather bag he was carrying.
10067{_}4664{_}"This is Mr. Lester, Mr. Shearrow," he added, and we shook hands.
10067{_}4665{_}"The object of this conference, Lester," he concluded, "is to straighten out certain matters connected with the Michaelovitch diamonds--and incidentally to give the _Record_ the biggest scoop it has had for months."
10067{_}4666{_}"I ain't here to fix up no scoop for the _Record_", broke in Grady.
10067{_}4667{_}"That paper never did treat me right."
10067{_}4668{_}"It has treated you as well as you deserved," retorted Godfrey.
10067{_}4669{_}"I'm going to talk plainly to you, Grady.
10067{_}4670{_}Your goose is cooked.
10067{_}4671{_}You can't hold on for an hour after last night's get-away becomes public."
10067{_}4672{_}"We'll see about that!"
10067{_}4673{_}growled Grady, but the fight had evidently been taken out of him.
10067{_}4674{_}"I understand you wouldn't let Simmonds telephone for me last night?"
10067{_}4675{_}queried Godfrey.
10067{_}4676{_}"That's right--it wasn't none of your business."
10067{_}4677{_}"Perhaps not.
10067{_}4678{_}And yet, if I had been there, the cleverest thief in Paris, if not in the world, would be safe behind those chrome-nickle steel bars at the Twenty-third Street station, instead of at liberty to go ahead and rob somebody else."
10067{_}4679{_}"You're mighty cocksure," retorted Grady.
10067{_}4680{_}"It's easy to be wise after it's all over."
10067{_}4681{_}"Well, I'm not going to argue with you," said Godfrey.
10067{_}4682{_}"I admit it was a good disguise, and a clever idea--but, just the same, you ought to have seen through it.
10067{_}4683{_}That's your business."
10067{_}4684{_}Grady mopped his face.
10067{_}4685{_}"Oh, of course!"
10067{_}4686{_}he sneered.
10067{_}4687{_}"I ought to have seen through it!
10067{_}4688{_}I ought to have suspected, even when I found you tryin' to interview him; even when I got him off the boat myself; even when I went through his papers and found them all right--yes, even to the photograph on his passport!
10067{_}4689{_}That's plain enough now, ain't it!
10067{_}4690{_}If people only had as good foresight as they have hindsight, how easy it would be!"
10067{_}4691{_}"Look here, Grady," said Godfrey, more kindly, "I haven't anything against you personally, and I admit that it was foolish of me to stand there talking to Crochard and never suspect who he was.
10067{_}4692{_}But that's all beside the mark.
10067{_}4693{_}You're at the head of the detective bureau, and you're the man who is responsible for all this.
10067{_}4694{_}You're energetic enough and all that; but you're not fit for your job--it's too big for you, and you know it.
10067{_}4695{_}Take my advice, and go to the 'phone there and send in your resignation."
10067{_}4696{_}Grady stared at him as though unable to believe his ears.
10067{_}4697{_}"'Phone in my resignation!"
10067{_}4698{_}he echoed.
10067{_}4699{_}"What kind of a fool do you think I am?"
10067{_}4700{_}"I see you're a bigger one than I thought you were!
10067{_}4701{_}Your pull can't help you any longer, Grady."
10067{_}4702{_}"Was it to tell me that you got me over here?"
10067{_}4703{_}"No," said Godfrey, "all this is just incidental--you began the discussion yourself, didn't you?
10067{_}4704{_}I got you here to meet...."  The outer door opened again, and Godfrey looked toward it, smiling.
10067{_}4705{_}"Moosseer Piggott!"
10067{_}4706{_}announced the office-boy.
10067{_}4707{_}And then I almost bounced from my seat, for I would have sworn that the man who stood on the threshold was the man who had opened the secret drawer.
10067{_}4708{_}He came forward, looking from face to face; then his eyes met Godfrey's and he smiled.
10067{_}4709{_}"Behold that I am here, monsieur," he said and I started anew at the voice, for it was the voice of Crochard.
10067{_}4710{_}"I hope that I have not kept you waiting."
10067{_}4711{_}"Not at all, M. Pigot," Godfrey assured him, and placed a chair for him.
10067{_}4712{_}I could see Grady and Simmonds gripping the arms of their chairs and staring at the newcomer, their mouths open; and I knew the thought that was flashing through their brains.
10067{_}4713{_}Was this Pigot?
10067{_}4714{_}Or was the man who had opened the cabinet Pigot?
10067{_}4715{_}Or was neither Pigot?
10067{_}4716{_}Was it possible that this could be a different man than the one who had opened the cabinet?
10067{_}4717{_}I confess that some such thought flashed through my own mind--a suspicion that Godfrey, in some way, was playing with us.
10067{_}4718{_}Godfrey looked about at us, smiling as he saw our expressions.
10067{_}4719{_}"I went down the bay this morning and met the _Savoie_," he said.
10067{_}4720{_}"I related to M. Pigot last night's occurrences, and begged him to be present at this meeting.
10067{_}4721{_}He was good enough to agree.
10067{_}4722{_}I assure you," he added, seeing Grady's look, "that this _is_ M. Pigot, of the Paris _Service du Surete,_ and not Crochard."
10067{_}4723{_}"Oh, yes," said M. Pigot, with a deprecating shrug.
10067{_}4724{_}"I am myself--and greatly humiliated that I should have fallen so readily into the trap which Crochard set for me.
10067{_}4725{_}But he is a very clever man."
10067{_}4726{_}"It was certainly a marvellous disguise," I said.
10067{_}4727{_}"It was more than that--it was an impersonation."
10067{_}4728{_}"Crochard has had occasion to study me," explained M. Pigot, drily.
10067{_}4729{_}"And he is an artist in whatever he does.
10067{_}4730{_}But some day I shall get him--every pitcher to the well goes once too often.
10067{_}4731{_}There is no hope of finding him here in New York?"
10067{_}4732{_}"I am afraid not," said Godfrey.
10067{_}4733{_}"Don't be too sure of that!"
10067{_}4734{_}broke in Grady ponderously.
10067{_}4735{_}"I ain't done yet--not by no manner of means!"
10067{_}4736{_}"Pardon me for not introducing you, M. Pigot," said Godfrey.
10067{_}4737{_}"This gentleman is Mr. Grady, who has been the head of our detective bureau; this is Mr. Simmonds, a member of his staff; this is Mr. Lester, an attorney and friend of mine; and this is Mr. Shearrow, my personal counsel.
10067{_}4738{_}Mr. Grady, Mr. Simmonds and Mr. Lester were present, last night," he added blandly, "when Crochard opened the secret drawer."
10067{_}4739{_}Grady reddened visibly, and even I felt my face grow hot.
10067{_}4740{_}M. Pigot looked at us with a smile of amusement.
10067{_}4741{_}"It must have been a most interesting experience," he said, "to have seen Crochard at work.
10067{_}4742{_}I have never had that privilege.
10067{_}4743{_}But I regret that he should have made good his escape."
10067{_}4744{_}"More especially since he took the Michaelovitch diamonds with him," I added.
10067{_}4745{_}"Before we go into that," said Godfrey, with a little smile, "there are one or two questions I should like to ask you, M. Pigot, in order to clear up some minor details which are as yet a little obscure.
10067{_}4746{_}Is it true that the theft of the Michaelovitch diamonds was planned by Crochard?"
10067{_}4747{_}"Undoubtedly.
10067{_}4748{_}No other thief in France would be capable of it."
10067{_}4749{_}"Is it also true that no direct evidence could be found against him?"
10067{_}4750{_}"That also is true, monsieur.
10067{_}4751{_}He had arranged the affair so cleverly that we were wholly unable to convict him, unless we should find him with the stolen brilliants in his possession."
10067{_}4752{_}"And you were not able to do that?"
10067{_}4753{_}"No; we could discover no trace of the brilliants, though we searched for them everywhere."
10067{_}4754{_}"But you did not know of the Boule cabinet and of the secret drawer?"
10067{_}4755{_}"No; of that we knew nothing.
10067{_}4756{_}I must examine that famous cabinet."
10067{_}4757{_}"It is worth examining.
10067{_}4758{_}And it has an interesting history.
10067{_}4759{_}But you did know, of course, that Crochard would seek a market for the diamonds here in America?"
10067{_}4760{_}"We knew that he would try to do so, and we did everything in our power to prevent it.
10067{_}4761{_}We especially relied upon your customs department to search most thoroughly the belongings of every person with whom they were not personally acquainted."
10067{_}4762{_}"The customs people did their part," said Godfrey with a chuckle.
10067{_}4763{_}"They have quite upset the country!
10067{_}4764{_}But the diamonds got in, in spite of them.
10067{_}4765{_}For, of course, a cabinet imported by a man so well known and so above suspicion as Mr. Vantine was passed without question!"
10067{_}4766{_}"Yes," agreed M. Pigot, a little bitterly.
10067{_}4767{_}"It was a most clever plan; and now, no doubt, Crochard can sell the brilliants at his leisure."
10067{_}4768{_}"Not if you've got a good description of them," protested Grady.
10067{_}4769{_}"I'll make it a point to warn every dealer in the country; I'll keep my whole force on the job; I'll get Chief Wilkie to lend me some of his men...."  "Oh, there is no use taking all that trouble," broke in Godfrey, negligently.
10067{_}4770{_}"Crochard won't try to sell them."
10067{_}4771{_}"Won't try to sell them?"
10067{_}4772{_}echoed Grady.
10067{_}4773{_}"What's the reason he won't?"
10067{_}4774{_}"Because he hasn't got them," answered Godfrey, smiling with an evidently deep enjoyment of Grady's dazed countenance.
10067{_}4775{_}"Oh, come off!"
10067{_}4776{_}said that worthy disgustedly.
10067{_}4777{_}"If he hasn't got 'em I'd like to know who has!"
10067{_}4778{_}"I have," said Godfrey, and cleared my desk with a sweep of his arm.
10067{_}4779{_}"Spread out your handkerchief, Lester," and as I dazedly obeyed, he picked up the little leather bag, opened it, and poured out its contents in a sparkling flood.
10067{_}4780{_}"There," he added, turning to Grady, "are the Michaelovitch diamonds."
10067{_}4781{_}CHAPTER XXVIII  CROCHARD WRITES AN EPILOGUE   For an instant, we gazed at the glittering heap with dazzled eyes; then Grady, with an inarticulate cry, sprang to his feet and picked up a handful of the diamonds, as though to convince himself of their reality.
10067{_}4782{_}"But I don't understand!"
10067{_}4783{_}he gasped.
10067{_}4784{_}"Have you got Croshar too?"
10067{_}4785{_}"No such luck," said Godfrey.
10067{_}4786{_}"Do you mean to say he'd give these up without a fight!"
10067{_}4787{_}The same thought was in my own mind; if Godfrey had run down Crochard and got the diamonds, without a life-and-death struggle, that engaging rascal must be much less formidable than I had supposed.
10067{_}4788{_}"My dear Grady," said Godfrey, "I haven't seen Crochard since the minute you took him off the boat.
10067{_}4789{_}I'd have had him, if you had let Simmonds call me.
10067{_}4790{_}That's what I had planned.
10067{_}4791{_}But he was too clever for us.
10067{_}4792{_}I knew that he would come to-day...."  "You knew that he would come to-day?"
10067{_}4793{_}repeated Grady blankly.
10067{_}4794{_}"How did you know that--or is it merely hot air?"
10067{_}4795{_}"I knew that he would come," said Godfrey, curtly, "because he wrote and told me so."
10067{_}4796{_}M. Pigot laughed a dry little laugh.
10067{_}4797{_}"That is a favourite device of his," he said; "and he always keeps his word."
10067{_}4798{_}"The trouble was," continued Godfrey, "that I didn't look for him so early in the day, and so he was able to send me on a wild-goose chase after a sensation that didn't exist.
10067{_}4799{_}There's where I was a fool.
10067{_}4800{_}But I discovered the secret drawer ten days ago--while the cabinet was still at Vantine's--the evening after the veiled lady got her letters.
10067{_}4801{_}It was easy enough.
10067{_}4802{_}I am surprised you didn't think of it, Lester."
10067{_}4803{_}"Think of what?"
10067{_}4804{_}I asked.
10067{_}4805{_}"Of the key to the mystery.
10067{_}4806{_}The drawer containing the letters was on the left side of the desk; I saw at once that there must be another drawer, opened in the same way, on the right side."
10067{_}4807{_}"I didn't see it," I said.
10067{_}4808{_}"I don't see it yet."
10067{_}4809{_}"Think a minute.
10067{_}4810{_}Why was Drouet killed?
10067{_}4811{_}Because he opened the wrong drawer.
10067{_}4812{_}He pressed the combination at the right side of the desk, instead of that at the left side.
10067{_}4813{_}The fair Julie must have thought the drawer was on the right side, instead of the left.
10067{_}4814{_}It was a mistake very easy to make, since her mistress doubtless had her back turned when Julie saw her open the drawer.
10067{_}4815{_}The suspicion that it was Julie's mistake becomes certainty when she shows the combination to Vantine, and he is killed, too.
10067{_}4816{_}Besides, the veiled lady herself made a remark which revealed the whole story."
10067{_}4817{_}"I didn't notice it," I said, resignedly.
10067{_}4818{_}"What was it?"
10067{_}4819{_}"That she was accustomed to opening the drawer with her left hand, instead of with her right.
10067{_}4820{_}After that, there could be no further doubt.
10067{_}4821{_}So I discovered the drawer very simply.
10067{_}4822{_}It had to be there."
10067{_}4823{_}"Yes," I said; "and then?"
10067{_}4824{_}"Then I removed the jewels, took them down to a dealer in paste gems and duplicated them as closely as I could.
10067{_}4825{_}I had a hard time getting a good copy of this big rose-diamond."
10067{_}4826{_}He picked it from the heap and held it up between his fingers.
10067{_}4827{_}"It's a beauty, isn't it?"
10067{_}4828{_}he asked.
10067{_}4829{_}M. Pigot smiled a dry smile.
10067{_}4830{_}"It is the Mazarin," he said, "and is worth three million francs.
10067{_}4831{_}There is a copy of it at the Louvre."
10067{_}4832{_}"So that's true, is it?"
10067{_}4833{_}I asked.
10067{_}4834{_}"Crochard told us the story."
10067{_}4835{_}"It is unquestionably true," said M. Pigot.
10067{_}4836{_}"It is not a secret--it is merely something which every one has forgotten."
10067{_}4837{_}"Well," continued Godfrey, "after I got the duplicates, I rolled them up in the cotton packets, and placed them back in the drawer, being careful to put the Mazarin at the bottom, where I had found it."
10067{_}4838{_}"It was lucky you thought of that," I said, "or Crochard would have suspected something."
10067{_}4839{_}Godfrey looked at me with a smile.
10067{_}4840{_}"My dear Lester," he said, "he knew that the game was up the instant he opened the first packet.
10067{_}4841{_}Do you suppose he would be deceived?
10067{_}4842{_}Not by the best reproduction ever made!"
10067{_}4843{_}And then I remembered the slow flush which had crept into Crochard's cheeks as he opened that first packet!
10067{_}4844{_}"I didn't expect to deceive him," Godfrey explained.
10067{_}4845{_}"I just wanted to give him a little surprise.
10067{_}4846{_}And to think I wasn't there to see it!"
10067{_}4847{_}"But if he knew they were imitations," I protested, "why should he go to all that trouble to steal them?"
10067{_}4848{_}"That is what puzzled me last night," said Godfrey; "and, for that matter, it puzzles me yet."
10067{_}4849{_}"Maybe he's got the real stones, after all," suggested Grady, who had been listening to all this with incredulous countenance.
10067{_}4850{_}"The story sounds fishy to me.
10067{_}4851{_}Maybe these are the imitations."
10067{_}4852{_}M. Pigot came forward and picked up the Mazarin and looked at it.
10067{_}4853{_}"This one, at least, is real," he said, after a moment.
10067{_}4854{_}"And I have no doubt the others are," he added, turning them over with his finger.
10067{_}4855{_}Grady, still incredulous, picked up one of the brilliants, went to the window, and drew it down the pane.
10067{_}4856{_}It left a deep scratch behind it.
10067{_}4857{_}"Yes," he admitted reluctantly, "I guess they're diamonds, all right," and he sat down again.
10067{_}4858{_}"And now, gentlemen," continued Godfrey, who had watched Grady's byplay with a tolerant smile, "I am ready to turn these diamonds over to you.
10067{_}4859{_}I should like you to count them, and give me a receipt for them."
10067{_}4860{_}"And then, of course, you will write the story," sneered Grady, "and give yourself all the credit."
10067{_}4861{_}"Well," asked Godfrey, looking at him, "do you think you deserve any?"
10067{_}4862{_}And Grady could only crimson and keep silent.
10067{_}4863{_}"As for the story, it is already written.
10067{_}4864{_}It will be on the streets in ten minutes--and it will create a sensation.
10067{_}4865{_}Please count the diamonds.
10067{_}4866{_}You will find two hundred and ten of them."
10067{_}4867{_}"That is the exact number stolen from the Grand Duke," remarked M. Pigot, and fell to counting.
10067{_}4868{_}The number was two hundred and ten.
10067{_}4869{_}"Mr. Shearrow has the receipt," Godfrey added, and Shearrow took a paper from his pocket, unfolded it, and read the contents.
10067{_}4870{_}It proved to be not only a receipt, but a full statement of the facts of the case, without omitting the details of the robbery and the credit due the _Record_ for the recovery of the diamonds.
10067{_}4871{_}Grady's face grew redder and redder as the reading proceeded.
10067{_}4872{_}"I won't sign no such testimonial as that," he blustered.
10067{_}4873{_}"Not on your life I won't!"
10067{_}4874{_}"You will sign it, will you not, M.
10067{_}4875{_}Pigot?"
10067{_}4876{_}asked Godfrey.
10067{_}4877{_}"Certainly," said the Frenchman; "it is a recognition of your services very well deserved," and he stepped forward and signed it with a flourish.
10067{_}4878{_}"Now, Simmonds," said Godfrey.
10067{_}4879{_}"No you don't!"
10067{_}4880{_}broke in Grady.
10067{_}4881{_}"Stay where you are, Simmonds.
10067{_}4882{_}I forbid you to sign that.
10067{_}4883{_}Remember, I'm your superior officer."
10067{_}4884{_}"No, he's not, Simmonds," said Godfrey, quietly.
10067{_}4885{_}"He hasn't been an officer at all for an hour and more."
10067{_}4886{_}Grady sprang to his feet, his eyes blazing, and strode toward Godfrey.
10067{_}4887{_}"What do you mean by that?"
10067{_}4888{_}he shouted.
10067{_}4889{_}"I mean," said Godfrey, looking him squarely in the eye, "that Mr. Shearrow and myself had a talk with the mayor this morning, and laid before him certain evidence in our possession--this latest case among others--and that your resignation was accepted at noon to-day."
10067{_}4890{_}"My resignation!"
10067{_}4891{_}snorted Grady.
10067{_}4892{_}"I never wrote one!"
10067{_}4893{_}"Tell the public that, if you want to," retorted Godfrey coldly.
10067{_}4894{_}"That's your affair.
10067{_}4895{_}You ought to have 'phoned it in when I told you to.
10067{_}4896{_}Now, Simmonds."
10067{_}4897{_}Grady stood glaring about him an instant, like an enraged bull, and I half expected him to hurl himself on Godfrey; instead, he crushed his hat upon his head, strode to the door, jerked it open, and banged it behind him.
10067{_}4898{_}"Now, Simmonds," Godfrey repeated, as the echo died away, and Simmonds came forward and signed.
10067{_}4899{_}I witnessed the signatures, and Godfrey, with more eagerness than he had shown in the whole affair, caught up the paper and sprang with it to the door.
10067{_}4900{_}"Get that down to the office, as quick as you can," he said, to a man outside.
10067{_}4901{_}"I'll 'phone instructions.
10067{_}4902{_}That," he added, closing the door and turning back to us, "is my reward for all this--or, rather, the _Record's_ reward.
10067{_}4903{_}And now, gentlemen, Mr. Shearrow has his car below, and I think we would better drive around to some safe-deposit box with this plunder."
10067{_}4904{_}It was perhaps ten days afterwards that Godfrey dropped in to see me one evening.
10067{_}4905{_}I was just back from a week on Cape Cod, which had done me a world of good; and, I need hardly say, was glad to see him.
10067{_}4906{_}"You're looking normal again," he said, surveying me, as he sat down.
10067{_}4907{_}"I was worried about you for a while."
10067{_}4908{_}"I never felt better.
10067{_}4909{_}I told you that all I needed was to have that mystery solved."
10067{_}4910{_}"And it was solved on schedule time, wasn't it," he smiled; "though not quite in the way I had anticipated.
10067{_}4911{_}Do you know, Lester," he added, "I am going to claim that cabinet."
10067{_}4912{_}"On what grounds?"
10067{_}4913{_}I demanded.
10067{_}4914{_}"Because the man who owned it gave it to me," and he got a paper out of his pocket-book and handed it across to me.
10067{_}4915{_}I opened it and recognised the delicate and feminine writing which I had seen once before.
10067{_}4916{_}"_My dear sir_ [the letter ran]:       "I find that I made the mistake of underestimating you, and I       present you my sincere apologies.
10067{_}4917{_}I trust that, at some future       time, it may be my privilege to be again engaged with you--the       result is certain to be most interesting.
10067{_}4918{_}But at present I find       that I must return to Europe by _La Bretagne_; since, after the       trouble I have taken, it is impossible that I should consent to       part with the brilliants of His Highness the Grand Duke.
10067{_}4919{_}As a       slight souvenir of my high regard, I trust you will be willing       to accept the cabinet Boule, which I am certain that good M.       Lester will surrender to you if you will show to him this letter.
10067{_}4920{_}The cabinet is not only interesting in itself, but will be doubly       so to you because of the part it has played in our little comedy.
10067{_}4921{_}And I should like to know that it adorns a corner of your home.
10067{_}4922{_}"Till we meet again, dear sir, believe me       "Your sincere admirer,       "CROCHARD, L'Invincible!"
10067{_}4923{_}"He's a good sport, isn't he?"
10067{_}4924{_}asked Godfrey, as I silently handed the letter back to him.
10067{_}4925{_}"What do you say about the cabinet?"
10067{_}4926{_}"I suppose there is no doubt that Crochard bought it," I said.
