10067{_}4927{_}"So that it is mine now?"
10067{_}4928{_}"Yes; but I'm going to solicit a bribe."
10067{_}4929{_}"Go ahead and solicit it."
10067{_}4930{_}"I want a souvenir, too," I said.
10067{_}4931{_}"I'd like awfully well to have that letter--besides," I added, "it will be a kind of receipt, you know, if anybody ever questions my giving you the cabinet."
10067{_}4932{_}Godfrey laughed and threw the letter across the table to me.
10067{_}4933{_}"It's yours," he said.
10067{_}4934{_}"And I'll send for the cabinet to-morrow.
10067{_}4935{_}I suppose it is still at the station?"
10067{_}4936{_}"Yes; I haven't had time to put in a claim for it.
10067{_}4937{_}But, Godfrey," I added, "when did _La Bretagne_ sail?"
10067{_}4938{_}"A week ago to-day.
10067{_}4939{_}She is due at Havre in the morning."
10067{_}4940{_}"Did you warn them?"
10067{_}4941{_}"Warn them of what?"
10067{_}4942{_}"That Crochard is after the diamonds.
10067{_}4943{_}They went back on _La Bretagne_, I suppose?"
10067{_}4944{_}"Yes--and Pigot went with them.
10067{_}4945{_}So why should I warn any one?
10067{_}4946{_}Surely they know that Crochard will get those diamonds if he can.
10067{_}4947{_}It has become a sort of point of honour with him, I imagine.
10067{_}4948{_}It is up to them to take care of them."
10067{_}4949{_}"That oughtn't to be difficult," I said.
10067{_}4950{_}"The strong-room of a liner is about the safest place on earth."
10067{_}4951{_}"Yes," Godfrey agreed, and blew a meditative ring toward the ceiling.
10067{_}4952{_}And presently he went away without saying anything more.
10067{_}4953{_}But the more I thought of it, the more the inflection he had given that word seemed an interrogation rather than an affirmation.
10067{_}4954{_}And when I opened my paper next morning, I more than half expected to be greeted with a black headline announcing the looting of the strong-room of _La Bretagne_.
10067{_}4955{_}But there was no such headline, and with a sigh, half of relief and half of disappointment, I turned to the other news.
10067{_}4956{_}But two weeks later, a black headline _did_ catch my eye:       MICHAELOVITCH JEWELS FALSE!
10067{_}4957{_}FRENCH DETECTIVE TAKES BACK PASTE IMITATIONS FROM AMERICA.
10067{_}4958{_}Fraud Discovered When the Grand Duke Michael Sends them to a      Jeweller to be Reset.
10067{_}4959{_}I had no need to read the article which followed, for I saw in a flash what had occurred.
10067{_}4960{_}I saw, too, why Crochard had retained the paste jewels--he had a use for them!
10067{_}4961{_}How or where the substitution had been made, I could only guess; but one thing was certain: the two weeks which had elapsed before the theft was discovered had given him ample opportunity to dispose of his plunder.
10067{_}4962{_}I felt sorry for the Grand Duke; sorrier still for that admirable M. Pigot; but, after all, one could not but admire the cleverness of the man who had despoiled them.
10067{_}4963{_}Who, I wondered, had bought the Mazarin?
10067{_}4964{_}Surely there was a diamond most difficult to sell.
10067{_}4965{_}It could, of course, be cut up--- but that would be sacrilege!
10067{_}4966{_}That question was answered, before long, in an unexpected way--a way which filled many columns in the papers, which delighted the comedy-loving French, and which gave Crochard a unique advertisement.
10067{_}4967{_}One morning, in the personal column of _Le Matin_, appeared a notice, of which this is the English:       "To M. the Director of the Museum of the Louvre:       "It has been my good fortune to come into possession of the       rose-diamond known as the Mazarin.
10067{_}4968{_}It is my wish to restore it       to your collection, in order that it may no longer be necessary       to delude the public with an imitation of coloured glass.
10067{_}4969{_}It will       give me great pleasure to present this brilliant to you, with my       compliments, provided His Highness, the Grand Duke Michael, who       preceded me in possession of the diamond, will join me in the gift.
10067{_}4970{_}Should he refuse, it will be my melancholy duty to cleave the       diamond into a number of smaller stones, as it is too large for       my use.
10067{_}4971{_}But I hope that he will not refuse.
10067{_}4972{_}"CROCHARD, L'Invincible!"
10067{_}4973{_}What could the Grand Duke do?
10067{_}4974{_}To have refused, would have made him the butt of the boulevards.
10067{_}4975{_}Besides, he was, after all, losing nothing which he had not already lost.
10067{_}4976{_}So, with a better grace than one might have expected, he consented to join in the restoration.
10067{_}4977{_}Two days later, the director of the Louvre discovered a packet upon his desk.
10067{_}4978{_}He opened it and found within the Mazarin.
10067{_}4979{_}When you visit the Louvre, you will see it in the place of honour in the glass case in the centre of the Gallery of Apollo, with an attendant on guard beside it.
10067{_}4980{_}But already the circumstances of its restoration are fading from the public memory.
10067{_}4981{_}And Crochard?
10067{_}4982{_}I do not know.
10067{_}4983{_}Each morning, I read first the news from Paris, searching for L'Invincible in some new incarnation.
10067{_}4984{_}I have his letter framed and hanging above my desk, and every day I read it over.
10067{_}4985{_}One sentence, especially, is forever running in my head:       "I trust that, at some future time, it may be my privilege to be       again engaged with you--the result is certain to be most       interesting."
10067{_}4986{_}And I trust that it may be my privilege, also, to be present at that engagement!

10067{_}5113{_}The path is based on the etext number (which is identical to the filename).
10067{_}5114{_}The path to the file is made up of single digits corresponding to all but the last digit in the filename.
10067{_}5115{_}For example an eBook of filename 10234 would be found at:       http://www.gutenberg.net/1/0/2/3/10234  or filename 24689 would be found at:      http://www.gutenberg.net/2/4/6/8/24689  An alternative method of locating eBooks:      http://www.gutenberg.net/GUTINDEX.ALL
